### US-045: Document the future structured-output widening (non-goal boundary)
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done ‚Äî verify-and-formalize: the widening is now documented as a deliberate non-goal seam in all three places (ADR-0007 Alternatives, CONTEXT "Ingestion boundary", `docs/ingestion-parser-adapters.md`), each US-045-tagged; AC3 re-verified via the US-036 grep + `test_parsing_seam.py`. Verified 2026-06-22.
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] ADR-0007 (already) + CONTEXT record that widening the boundary's output type to carry structure (tables/bboxes/layout) for a layout-aware chunker is a **future** change that touches `chunking.py`, explicitly not built in v1. *(ADR-0007 ¬ß"Alternatives considered and rejected" ‚Üí "Widen the boundary output type now to carry structure (tables / bounding boxes / layout) ‚Ä¶ Rejected for v1 ‚Ä¶ also touches `chunking.py` ‚Ä¶ a deliberate v1 pin with a known upgrade path (US-045)". CONTEXT "Ingestion boundary" ‚Üí "Markdown-string output contract (v1, pinned)" bullet, now tagged "future change (US-045) that also touches `chunking.py` ‚Äî explicitly not v1".)*
- [x] The "write your own adapter" guide (US-043) references this so an author understands why `parse` returns `str` today. *(`docs/ingestion-parser-adapters.md` ‚Üí the "Why `str` and not something richer?" blockquote under "The one rule" ("‚Ä¶a future *layout-aware* chunker‚Ä¶ also rewrites `chunking.py` ‚Äî it is out of v1 (ADR-0007 ‚Üí US-045). Do not try to return a non-`str` today"), reinforced by the F3 matrix "Markdown-string ceiling" row and the closing checklist item.)*
- [x] No v1 code carries a non-`str` document type across the boundary (consistent with US-036's verification). *(Re-ran the US-036 grep ‚Äî docling confined to `backend/parsing.py` only; `chunking.py` has 0 docling refs; all three `DocumentParser.parse` impls return `-> str`; `backend/test_parsing_seam.py` green ‚Äî 3/3 checks.)*
**Validation Test:**
- **Setup:** Read ADR-0007 + CONTEXT "Ingestion boundary" + the authoring guide.
- **Steps:** 1. Confirm each states the markdown-string pin and the future widening. 2. Re-run US-036's grep to confirm no non-`str` document type crosses the seam in v1.
- **Expected Result:** The pin and its future upgrade path are documented in all three places; v1 code holds the `str` contract.
- **Failure Indicator:** The widening is undocumented (looks like a limitation, not a decision), or v1 code already leaks a structured type across the boundary.

#### Functional requirements (this area)
- FR-I1: docling is imported in exactly one backend module (`backend/parsing.py`); the chunker (`backend/chunking.py`) consumes only a `str` ‚Äî verifiable by grep/import check (I5, verified not refactored).
- FR-I2: A one-method `DocumentParser` ABC defines the boundary: `parse(raw: bytes, filename: str, content_type: str | None) -> str`, output normalized markdown string (v1, pinned), mirroring `Reranker` / `WebSearchProvider`.
- FR-I3: `build_parser` + `PARSER=docling|unstructured|llamaparse` selects the parser; default `docling`; invalid value fails fast; commercial adapters raise at build time on a missing API key.
- FR-I4: `DoclingParser` is the default adapter; the `pypdfium2` PDF fallback stays inside it (not promoted to the boundary).
- FR-I5: A real working `LlamaParseParser` adapter ships behind the protocol (OCR/complex-layout escape hatch), with a real-round-trip smoke test that runs on a key and skips without one.
- FR-I6: Any adapter's markdown output feeds `chunk_text` with no parser-specific branch (the markdown-string contract is the only coupling).
- FR-I7: A "write your own adapter" guide documents subclass + register + select + the must-flatten-to-markdown rule, names Unstructured.io as the canonical BYO example, and points at the LlamaParse smoke test as the proof template.
- FR-I8: Accepted gaps (OCR-not-default, markdown-string ceiling, unstructured-is-BYO) are recorded as F3 rows citing ADR-0007.

#### Non-goals (this area)
- A layout-aware / structured (non-markdown) output contract ‚Äî widening `parse` to carry tables/bboxes/layout for a layout-aware chunker is a **documented future** change touching `chunking.py`, not v1.
- OCR / scanned / image-only document support **in the default parser** ‚Äî that is the LlamaParse adapter's job (PRD ¬ß3.3 out-of-scope for the default).
- Three documented stubs (Unstructured + LlamaParse + "yours") with no working adapter ‚Äî exactly one *real* working commercial adapter ships (LlamaParse); a stub would not prove the swap.
- A shipped working `Unstructured.io` adapter ‚Äî it remains a valid buyer-written adapter behind the same protocol, documented in the authoring guide, not built in v1.
- Multiple chunking strategies or any change to the heading-aware chunker ‚Äî the chunker stays markdown/`str`-only; this area does not touch chunking behavior.
- Re-threading / refactoring docling out of the pipeline ‚Äî there is nothing threaded to undo; I5 is verify-and-formalize only.
- Promoting the `pypdfium2` PDF fallback to the boundary ‚Äî it is a docling-path concern that stays inside `DoclingParser`.
## D. Escalation signal & deterministic deflection pipeline (ADR-0003)

The support face answers a customer or escalates to a human via a **deterministic deflection pipeline** ‚Äî `retrieve (hybrid, once) ‚Üí retrieval gate ‚Üí [if strong] draft ‚Üí faithfulness gate ‚Üí answer-or-escalate` ‚Äî never the built agentic tool loop (M1). The escalation signal is retrieval-grounded **OR** faithfulness-grounded, run as a cascade that exploits the OR's short-circuit: the cheap cosine-defined retrieval gate fires first (escalate with no draft, no judge call), and only strong-retrieval queries pay for a draft plus one fast faithfulness judge call. The decision is control flow, never a model `escalate()` tool. E7 is a three-population golden set (P1a/P1b unanswerable, P2 auto-resolve, P3 unfaithful) whose runner sweeps the three knobs to the deflection-maximizing knee under a buyer-set false-resolve ceiling; the deterministic retrieval-gate tripwire runs per-PR while the LLM-judge sweep runs scheduled.

### US-046: Surface pre-fusion raw cosine on retrieval results
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done ‚Äî `backend/retrieval.py` (`cosine_similarity` field + `search_documents` carry + `_rrf_fuse` preservation) + `backend/test_cosine_surface.py`; mypy clean, 5 test groups green (2026-06-22).
**Description:** As a platform engineer, I want `hybrid_search` to carry the pre-fusion raw cosine similarity on each result so that the retrieval gate can threshold "weak retrieval" on a calibrated `[0,1]` cosine instead of the RRF rank artifact.
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] `SearchDocumentsResult` in `backend/retrieval.py` gains a `cosine_similarity: float | None` field that carries the raw vector cosine from `match_chunks`; keyword-only rows (no embedding) carry `None` (`backend/retrieval.py`, around the `SearchDocumentsResult` model at line 137 and the `_rrf_fuse` copy at line 370). *(Field added with `= None` default; `search_documents` mirrors `match_chunks`' `similarity` onto it, `keyword_search` leaves the default.)*
- [x] `_rrf_fuse` no longer loses the cosine: when it overwrites `similarity` with the summed RRF score (`model_copy(update={"similarity": ...})`), it preserves the vector side's `cosine_similarity` for each fused row (carried from the vector ranking's row, `None` when a chunk appeared only in the keyword ranking). *(A `cosine_by_id` map takes the first non-None cosine ‚Äî vector ranking is iterated first, so its cosine wins; the fuse `model_copy` sets both `similarity` and `cosine_similarity` explicitly. Reranking, which also `model_copy`s only `similarity`, preserves the cosine for free.)*
- [x] `vector` and `keyword` modes are unaffected ‚Äî `search_documents` sets `cosine_similarity` equal to its `similarity` (both are cosine), `keyword_only_search` sets it `None`; the eval runner's metric blocks are byte-stable. *(The eval runner builds metric blocks from `r.id`‚Üístable_id, never serializing the model, so the additive field is inert there.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes *(mypy clean on `retrieval.py` + `test_cosine_surface.py`.)*
**Validation:** `backend/test_cosine_surface.py` drives the **real** `search_documents` / `keyword_search` / `hybrid_search` via an `httpx.MockTransport` (RPCs stubbed) + a fake embeddings client: vector rows `cosine == similarity ‚àà [0,1]`; keyword rows cosine `None`; hybrid fuses A(vector-only)/B(both)/C(keyword-only) ‚Üí small RRF `similarity` while A keeps 0.62, B keeps the vector-side 0.41, C is `None`, and `cosine != similarity` (the plumbing-bug guard). Plus a pure `_rrf_fuse` determinism check.
**Validation Test:**
- **Setup:** Seed the e-commerce corpus; pick a query with both a strong vector hit and a strong keyword hit.
- **Steps:** 1. Call `hybrid_search` for the query. 2. Inspect the top fused row's `similarity` and `cosine_similarity`.
- **Expected Result:** `similarity` is the small RRF score (‚âà ‚â§0.033 at k=60); `cosine_similarity` is a distinct value in `[0,1]` matching what `search_documents` returns for the same chunk. A fused row that appeared only in the keyword ranking has `cosine_similarity is None`.
- **Failure Indicator:** `cosine_similarity` equals the RRF score, is absent, or is `None` for a chunk that was a vector hit ‚Äî the raw cosine was lost in fusion (the ADR-0003 plumbing bug).

### US-047: Cosine-defined retrieval gate (config knobs œÑ_sim, N)
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done ‚Äî net-new `backend/escalation.py` (`retrieval_gate` + frozen `RetrievalGateDecision`) + `backend/test_escalation_gate.py`; mypy clean, 8 test groups green (2026-06-22).
**Description:** As a support-platform operator, I want a deterministic retrieval gate that judges retrieval "weak" from raw cosine so that a query with no good context escalates before any draft or judge call is made.
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] New net-new module (e.g. `backend/escalation.py`) exposes a pure function `retrieval_gate(results, tau_sim, n_min, match_threshold) -> RetrievalGateDecision` returning `{strong: bool, top1_cosine: float | None, n_cleared: int, reason}`. *(`RetrievalGateDecision` is a frozen pydantic model mirroring the `ProviderConfig` convention; `reason` is a machine-stable tag ‚Äî every weak reason starts with `"weak"` ‚Äî for logging/eval only, never customer-facing.)*
- [x] "Weak" is defined exactly per ADR-0003: `strong = (top1_cosine >= tau_sim) AND (n_cleared >= n_min)`, where `top1_cosine` is the max `cosine_similarity` across results (US-046) and `n_cleared` counts rows whose `cosine_similarity >= match_threshold`. Empty results ‚áí weak. *(Both thresholds are inclusive `>=`; `None` cosines ‚Äî keyword-only rows ‚Äî are excluded from `top1_cosine`/`n_cleared`, so a results list with no vector cosine is weak with `top1_cosine=None`.)*
- [x] The gate reads only `cosine_similarity` (never `similarity`/RRF) and is **pure arithmetic on scores** ‚Äî no LLM, no reranker dependency. It survives deletion of the optional reranker module (R4); a reranker, when present, may supply a calibrated score in place of cosine but the gate contract stays cosine. *(`escalation.py` imports only `SearchDocumentsResult` from `retrieval` ‚Äî nothing from `reranking`; range-validation of the knobs is deferred to US-050 config, keeping the gate total over any floats.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes *(mypy clean on `escalation.py` + `test_escalation_gate.py`.)*
**Validation:** `backend/test_escalation_gate.py` (pure, runs anywhere) covers the PRD cases (a) 0.62/4-rows ‚Üí strong, (b) 0.18 ‚Üí weak, (c) empty ‚Üí weak; plus determinism + frozen-immutability, the **failure-indicator guard** (a high-RRF/low-cosine row is weak and a real-hybrid small-RRF/high-cosine row is strong ‚Äî proving the gate reads cosine, not `similarity`), keyword-only-None weakness + exclusion from top1/n_cleared, the `n_min` count-miss boundary, and inclusive `>=` boundaries on both knobs.
**Validation Test:**
- **Setup:** Construct three `SearchDocumentsResult` lists: (a) top1 cosine 0.62 with 4 rows ‚â• threshold; (b) top1 cosine 0.18; (c) empty list. Use `tau_sim=0.4`, `n_min=2`, `match_threshold=0.3`.
- **Steps:** 1. Call `retrieval_gate` on each. 2. Read `.strong`.
- **Expected Result:** (a) `strong=True`; (b) `strong=False` (top1 below œÑ_sim); (c) `strong=False` (empty). Identical inputs always yield identical decisions.
- **Failure Indicator:** Any non-determinism, or the gate thresholding `similarity` (RRF) so a high-RRF/low-cosine query is wrongly called strong.

### US-048: One-call runtime faithfulness gate (net-new, latency path)
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done ‚Äî `backend/escalation.py` (`faithfulness_gate` + `FaithfulnessJudgment`/`FaithfulnessDecision` + `get_judge_model`) + `backend/test_faithfulness_gate.py`; mypy clean, 9 test groups green (2026-06-22).
**Description:** As a support-platform operator, I want a single structured-output judge call to verify a drafted answer is supported by its retrieved chunks so that a confidently-wrong answer is caught before it auto-sends.
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] Net-new `faithfulness_gate(draft, chunks, cutoff) -> FaithfulnessDecision` in the request latency path makes **exactly one** structured-output call returning `{supported: bool, score: float}` on a cheap/fast judge model (the ADR-0006 runtime judge role; `gpt-4o-mini` / `haiku`-class) ‚Äî **not** full RAGAS claim-decomposition. *(Signature adds the injected `judge_client` first, per the `extract_document_metadata` convention; one `chat.completions.parse` call with `response_format=FaithfulnessJudgment`. `get_judge_model()` reads `JUDGE_MODEL` ‚Üí default `gpt-4o-mini`, deliberately NOT chaining through `OPENAI_MODEL` so the latency-path judge stays cheap.)*
- [x] The decision is `supported AND score >= cutoff`; a judge error / parse failure / timeout fails **closed** (treated as unfaithful ‚áí escalate), never open. *(`cutoff` is inclusive `>=`; score clamped to `[0,1]`; every failure mode ‚Äî SDK/API error, timeout, refusal, empty choices, missing parsed payload ‚Äî routes through `_unfaithful(tag)` ‚Üí `faithful=False`. Test asserts the forced-exception case never fail-opens.)*
- [x] This code is explicitly distinct from the offline RAGAS faithfulness metric in `evals/retrieval/ragas.py` (which makes several calls, runs weekly); a code comment states "runtime gate, net-new ‚Äî not the offline RAGAS metric" so the same word "faithfulness" never conflates the two machineries. *(Banner comment above the gate + a paragraph in the module docstring, both naming `evals/retrieval/ragas.py`.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes *(mypy clean on `escalation.py` + `test_faithfulness_gate.py`.)*
**Validation:** `backend/test_faithfulness_gate.py` (pure, runs anywhere) drives the gate with a call-counting fake judge mirroring the SDK shape: grounded ‚Üí faithful, ungrounded ‚Üí escalate, **exactly one call** per evaluation, forced exception ‚Üí fail-closed (never fail-open), inclusive cutoff boundary, refusal/empty-choices/missing-payload fail-closed, score clamping, the `JUDGE_MODEL` selector (no `OPENAI_MODEL` chaining), draft+chunk content actually reaching the judge, and a frozen-decision check.
**Validation Test:**
- **Setup:** A draft fully grounded in two chunks, and a draft asserting a fact absent from its chunks. `cutoff=0.7`.
- **Steps:** 1. Run `faithfulness_gate` on each. 2. Count judge calls made. 3. Force a judge exception on a third call.
- **Expected Result:** Grounded draft ‚Üí `supported=True`, passes; ungrounded draft ‚Üí fails; exactly one judge call per evaluation; the forced-error case returns "unfaithful" (escalate).
- **Failure Indicator:** More than one judge call, a RAGAS-style multi-call decomposition, or a judge error defaulting to "faithful" (fail-open) and auto-sending.

### US-049: Deterministic deflection pipeline orchestrator
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done ‚Äî `backend/escalation.py` (`run_deflection_pipeline` + `draft_support_answer` + frozen `DeflectionResult` + `GENERIC_DEFERRAL`) + `backend/test_deflection_pipeline.py`; mypy clean, 5 test groups green (2026-06-22).
**Description:** As a customer using the support widget, I want my message answered or escalated by a deterministic pipeline so that the cheap retrieval gate short-circuits weak queries with no wasted draft and the model never decides on its own to resolve.
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] An orchestrator runs the exact ADR-0003 control flow: `retrieve (hybrid, once) ‚Üí retrieval gate ‚Üí [if strong] draft ‚Üí faithfulness gate ‚Üí answer-or-escalate`. It does **not** call the M1 agentic loop (`for _iteration in range(MAX_TOOL_ITERATIONS)`, now at `backend/main.py:1064` ‚Äî PRD's `:941` was stale, so the code cites the `MAX_TOOL_ITERATIONS` symbol); the shared machinery is retrieval + the gates ("one engine"), not the loop. *(`run_deflection_pipeline` calls `hybrid_search` once then `retrieval_gate`/`faithfulness_gate`; the draft is a single plain `chat.completions.create` with no `tools`. Test asserts both RPCs hit exactly once.)*
- [x] Short-circuit proven: when the retrieval gate returns weak, the orchestrator escalates having made **zero** draft-generation and **zero** faithfulness-judge calls (the OR's left operand decided it). *(Test counts the injected answerer/judge clients: weak path ‚Üí `create_calls == 0` and `parse_calls == 0`, `faithfulness is None`.)*
- [x] On escalate, the customer-facing output is the generic deferral ("a human will follow up") with **no** `reason`/access metadata; on answer, the drafted-and-faithful answer is returned. No `escalate()` tool is registered for the model ‚Äî the answer-vs-escalate decision is in deterministic control flow only. *(`_escalated` is the sole escalated-result constructor and always sets `customer_message = GENERIC_DEFERRAL`; the gate `reason`/scores live only on internal fields. Test asserts the reason/scores never appear in `customer_message`.)*
- [x] User-initiated "talk to a human" is out of scope here (a separate widget button owned by the support-surface section); reference it, do not implement it. *(Docstring references US-066+; no such button implemented.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes *(mypy clean on `escalation.py` + `test_deflection_pipeline.py`.)*
**Validation:** `backend/test_deflection_pipeline.py` drives the **real** orchestrator (hybrid retrieval via `httpx.MockTransport`, call-counting fake embedder/answerer/judge): off-topic‚Üíescalate with 0 draft + 0 judge calls (hybrid still ran once), supported‚Üíanswered with exactly 1 draft + 1 judge call and **no `tools`** on the draft call, strong-but-unfaithful‚Üíescalate (1+1, faithfulness recorded internally), empty-draft‚Üíescalate without a judge call, and a no-reason-leak assertion on every escalation plus a frozen-result check. **Note for US-050:** the orchestrator takes `tau_sim`/`n_min`/`match_threshold`/`faithfulness_cutoff` as explicit params (no env reads) ‚Äî US-050 will supply the validated global config + defaults the support endpoint passes in.
**Validation Test:**
- **Setup:** Two messages ‚Äî one with strong corpus support, one off-topic with no support ‚Äî against a seeded support bot. Instrument draft + judge call counts.
- **Steps:** 1. Run the off-topic message through the orchestrator. 2. Run the supported message. 3. Inspect call counts and outputs.
- **Expected Result:** Off-topic ‚Üí escalate, generic deferral, 0 draft calls, 0 judge calls. Supported ‚Üí drafted answer that passed the faithfulness gate (1 draft, 1 judge call). The agentic loop is never entered.
- **Failure Indicator:** A weak-retrieval query produces a draft or a judge call (short-circuit destroyed); the escalation output leaks a `reason`; or the pipeline routes through `MAX_TOOL_ITERATIONS`.

### US-050: Escalation config ‚Äî three global knobs + false-resolve ceiling
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done ‚Äî `backend/escalation.py` (`EscalationConfig` frozen value object + `from_env` + standalone `get_false_resolve_ceiling` + `_env_unit_float`/`_env_min_int` validators) + `backend/test_escalation_config.py`; mypy clean, 10 test groups green (2026-06-22).
**Description:** As a buyer, I want œÑ_sim, N, the faithfulness cutoff, and a false-resolve ceiling expressed as global config so that I set my risk tolerance with one number and the gate defaults come from the E7 sweep.
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] Three gate knobs (`ESCALATION_TAU_SIM`, `ESCALATION_N_MIN`, `ESCALATION_FAITHFULNESS_CUTOFF` or equivalent) are read as typed, validated global config with defaults sourced from the E7 sweep knee (US-058); validation rejects out-of-range values (`œÑ_sim`/cutoff ‚àà `[0,1]`, `N ‚â• 1`), mirroring `get_similarity_threshold` in `backend/retrieval.py`. *(Frozen `EscalationConfig(tau_sim, n_min, faithfulness_cutoff)` + `from_env()`; `_env_unit_float`/`_env_min_int` reuse the `get_similarity_threshold` parse‚Üírange-check‚Üí`ValueError`-naming-the-var shape. Defaults `0.4`/`2`/`0.7` are documented ADR-0003 placeholders until the US-058 knee promotes its recommended values. `Field(ge/le)` bounds make the object self-validating on direct construction too.)*
- [x] The **false-resolve ceiling** is a separate config value documented as "the one number a buyer sets as their risk tolerance"; it is consumed by the E7 sweep / knee selection (US-058) and the E8 gate (US-059), not by the per-request pipeline. *(`get_false_resolve_ceiling()` is a STANDALONE getter ‚Äî `ESCALATION_FALSE_RESOLVE_CEILING`, default `0.05` ‚Äî deliberately NOT a field on `EscalationConfig`, so it is structurally un-wireable into `run_deflection_pipeline`. A test asserts the config carries exactly the 3 gate knobs and no `*ceiling*` field/attr.)*
- [x] Per-workspace tuning is explicitly deferred but **config-shaped** ‚Äî a comment notes a future per-workspace override key resolved on top of the global default, no schema migration implied. *(Section comment: a future per-workspace `escalation_config` row resolves ON TOP OF the `from_env` global default ‚Äî read global, overlay workspace knobs ‚Äî no migration implied here; v1 is single global.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes *(mypy clean on `escalation.py` + `test_escalation_config.py`.)*
**Validation Test:**
- **Setup:** Set `ESCALATION_TAU_SIM=0.4`, `ESCALATION_N_MIN=2`, cutoff `0.7`; then set `œÑ_sim=1.5`.
- **Steps:** 1. Load config with valid values. 2. Load with `œÑ_sim=1.5`. 3. Confirm the pipeline reads these defaults.
- **Expected Result:** Valid config loads and the gate uses those values; `œÑ_sim=1.5` raises a clear validation error at startup; omitting all knobs yields the documented E7-derived defaults.
- **Failure Indicator:** Out-of-range knobs silently accepted, a knob hardcoded in the gate instead of config-driven, or the false-resolve ceiling wired into the per-request path.

P2-vs-P3 is the only human judgment ("does a faithful answer exist from these chunks?"). *(Loader enforces the anchor rule: `no_context` rows MUST carry no gold; `answerable_faithful`/`should_escalate` MUST carry a non-empty `gold_stable_ids` list of non-empty strings. The shipped set's P2/P3 rows are anchored to real chunks verified against `backend.chunking.chunk_text` boundaries ‚Äî e.g. P3 "jewelry warranty" ‚Üí `warranty-terms:0` (categories chunk lists Electronics/Apparel/Home Goods, not jewelry ‚Üí strong retrieval, no faithful answer).)*

The schema does not add a `P1b` label. *(No `p1b` value in `ESCALATION_LABELS`; a hand-authored `escalation: p1b` row is rejected as out-of-enum with a message stating P1b is the derived no-access case. - [x] Typecheck/lint passes *(`e7.py`/`test_e7.py` type-clean modulo the `import yaml` stub note shared by `runner.py`/`e6.py` ‚Äî the evals package carries no mypy gate and uses the same stubless-lib convention; no genuine type errors.)*

- **Expected Result:** Valid rows load with their labels; the invalid label raises a clear loader error naming the allowed enum.
- **Failure Indicator:** An out-of-enum label silently accepted, or a hand-written P1b row appearing in the set.

### US-052: E7 population P1a ‚Äî genuinely-no-context escalation
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done ‚Äî `evals/retrieval/e7_runner.py` (`run_e7_p1a` + `P1aDecision`/`E7P1aResult` + `render_e7_p1a_section` + standalone `python -m evals.retrieval.e7_runner` entry) + `evals/retrieval/test_e7_runner.py`; 8 offline test groups green, mypy-clean to the eval-package standard (2026-06-22).

**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] The E7 runner classifies a P1a row's outcome via the deterministic retrieval gate (US-047) reusing the real `backend` gate function ‚Äî a future PR that breaks the gate breaks E7 (same "real backend functions" discipline as `evals/retrieval/runner.py`). *(`run_e7_p1a` imports and calls `escalation.retrieval_gate` directly ‚Äî pure arithmetic on the pre-fusion cosine, no copy of the logic; the gate knobs come from the same `EscalationConfig.from_env()` + `retrieval.get_similarity_threshold()` the production support endpoint uses (US-050), so a buyer's knob change is reflected. `test_e7_runner.py` drives the **real** orchestrator + gate with a call-counting fake retriever ‚Äî the cosine-not-RRF test pins real-gate semantics.)*
- [x] P1a expected outcome is `escalate` with no draft/judge call; the runner records `top1_cosine` and `n_cleared` so a near-miss is visible in the JSON. *(A weak gate ‚áí `decision="escalate"`; the P1a leg has NO answerer/judge client at all, so "0 draft / 0 judge" is structural ‚Äî `draft_calls`/`judge_calls` are pinned 0 and surfaced per row. `P1aDecision` carries `top1_cosine`/`n_cleared`/`gate_reason` straight off the real gate decision ‚Äî the near-miss test asserts a `top1_cosine` just below `œÑ_sim` is recorded. A P1a row that CLEARS the gate is flagged `correct=False` (a retrieval-leg false-resolve risk) and fails the run with exit 1, AFTER the JSON is written ‚Äî same shape as E6's leak gate; an empty P1a population is NOT a pass, mirroring E6's positive control. Kept a standalone runner because the deterministic gate leg is the per-PR tripwire (US-059) and must not pay for the full E4 sweep + RAGAS.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes *(mypy-clean with the backend resolvable + the shared `yaml`/`asyncpg` stubless-lib convention, same standard as `runner.py`/`e6.py`/`e7.py`.)*

- **Steps:** 1. Run E7 over the P1a row. 2. Inspect its recorded decision.
- **Expected Result:** Decision `escalate`, caught at the retrieval gate, 0 draft/judge calls.
- **Failure Indicator:** P1a row drafted or auto-resolved (a false-resolve), or scored through a non-deterministic path.

### US-053: E7 population P2 ‚Äî answerable + faithful ‚Üí auto-resolve
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done ‚Äî `evals/retrieval/e7_runner.py` (`run_e7_p2` + `P2Decision`/`E7P2Result` + `render_e7_p2_section` + `_render_judge_context` + `--include-p2`/`--faithfulness-judge-min` CLI), `evals/retrieval/e7.py` (`_REFERENCED_LABELS` reference rule), `evals/retrieval/escalation_gold.yaml` (4 P2 rows now carry `reference`), `evals/retrieval/test_e7_runner.py` (8 new P2 groups, 16 total) + `evals/retrieval/test_e7.py` (9 groups, +reference rule); mypy/pyflakes clean to the eval-package standard (2026-06-22).
**Description:** As an eval author, I want P2 questions scored end-to-end so that I can measure the deflection rate on questions a faithful answer exists for.
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] P2 rows pass both gates: strong retrieval then a faithful draft; expected outcome `auto-resolve`. The faithfulness leg uses the offline RAGAS/cross-family infra (`evals/retrieval/ragas.py` + the Claude judge in `runner.py`) to **score** the gate, not the runtime one-call gate. *(`run_e7_p2` runs the pipeline shape `retrieve ‚Üí retrieval_gate ‚Üí [if strong] draft ‚Üí faithfulness scoring ‚Üí auto-resolve-or-escalate`, reusing the REAL backend `escalation.retrieval_gate` + `escalation.draft_support_answer`. Faithfulness is scored by the OFFLINE cross-family Claude judge `runner.judge_answer` (1-5 scale, injected as `Judge`, wired to `r.JUDGE_MODEL`=`claude-haiku-4-5`) ‚Äî explicitly NOT the runtime one-call `escalation.faithfulness_gate`. RAGAS's `score_with_ragas` is still a US-001 scaffold returning `[]`, so the load-bearing offline signal is the cross-family Claude judge it ships alongside. Auto-resolve = strong gate AND `faithfulness_score >= faithfulness_judge_min` (default 4 = "mostly grounded"; `--faithfulness-judge-min`, deliberately a DIFFERENT scale from the runtime gate's [0,1] `faithfulness_cutoff`). A test asserts the offline judge receives the `reference` the runtime gate never sees.)*
- [x] A P2 row that escalates is counted as a **false-escalate** (annoyance cost), tallied per US-055. *(Every P2 escalation sets `false_escalate=True` + `correct=False` and records `escalate_leg ‚àà {retrieval, draft, faithfulness}` so a regression is attributable; `E7P2Result.false_escalates` / `false_escalate_rate` / `deflection_rate` + the `false_escalates` id list in the JSON feed US-055's consolidated rates. P2 is a tunable quality metric, NOT a pinned invariant: a false-escalate is logged but never fails the run ‚Äî only the P1a safety invariant decides the exit code (US-059). The leg is `--include-p2` opt-in (needs `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`), LLM-judged, so it is a scheduled/weekly artifact, never a per-PR block.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes *(mypy clean on `e7_runner.py`/`e7.py` modulo the shared `yaml`/`asyncpg` stubless-lib note; pyflakes clean; 16 `test_e7_runner` groups + 9 `test_e7` groups green.)*
**Validation Test:**
- **Setup:** A P2 question with strong gold support and a hand-authored reference answer.
- **Steps:** 1. Run E7 over the P2 row. 2. Inspect the decision and faithfulness score.
- **Expected Result:** Decision `auto-resolve`; counted toward deflection; faithfulness score recorded.
- **Failure Indicator:** A faithfully-answerable P2 escalating without being counted as a false-escalate, or being scored by the runtime gate instead of the offline judge.

### US-054: E7 population P3 ‚Äî strong retrieval, no faithful answer ‚Üí escalate
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done ‚Äî `evals/retrieval/e7_runner.py` (shared `_run_judged_leg` traversal extracted from the P2 leg + `run_e7_p3`/`P3Decision`/`E7P3Result`/`render_e7_p3_section` + `--include-p3` CLI + loud false-resolve logging), `evals/retrieval/e7.py` (`should_escalate` added to `_REFERENCED_LABELS`), `evals/retrieval/escalation_gold.yaml` (3 P3 rows now carry a should-escalate `reference`), `evals/retrieval/test_e7_runner.py` (8 new P3 groups, 24 total) + `evals/retrieval/test_e7.py` (reference rule now covers P2+P3, 9 groups); pyflakes clean, mypy-clean to the eval-package `yaml`-stub standard (2026-06-22).
**Description:** As an eval author, I want P3 questions ‚Äî strong retrieval but no faithful grounded answer ‚Äî scored at the faithfulness gate so that the hardest, most important case (the moat) is proven.
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] P3 rows clear the retrieval gate (strong cosine) but the faithfulness leg must return unfaithful ‚áí expected outcome `escalate (faithfulness gate)`. The runner records both the gate decision and the offline faithfulness score. *(`run_e7_p3` runs the SAME shared deflection-pipeline traversal as P2 ‚Äî `_run_judged_leg`: retrieve ‚Üí real `escalation.retrieval_gate` ‚Üí real `escalation.draft_support_answer` ‚Üí OFFLINE cross-family Claude judge `runner.judge_answer` ‚Äî but labels the outcome with P3 semantics: `correct` iff the row escalated at the FAITHFULNESS leg. `P3Decision` carries the gate decision (`gate_strong`/`top1_cosine`/`n_cleared`/`gate_reason`) AND the offline `faithfulness_score`/`helpfulness_score`. P3 rows now require a `reference` ‚Äî the should-escalate gold the offline judge scores against ‚Äî enforced by the loader and shipped on all 3 gold rows.)*
- [x] A P3 row that auto-resolves is a **false-resolve** (the Risk #3 safety failure) and is tallied toward the false-resolve rate (US-055), which the ceiling governs. *(An `auto_resolve` decision sets `false_resolve=True` + `correct=False`; `E7P3Result.false_resolves` / `false_resolve_rate` + the `false_resolves` id list in the JSON feed US-055's consolidated rate. Surfaced at ERROR level in the standalone runner. Per US-059 the false-resolve RATE vs the buyer's ceiling is consolidated in US-055 and enforced in CI by US-059, NOT per-leg here ‚Äî this LLM-judged leg only reports, so it never changes this runner's exit code (the deterministic P1a invariant alone decides it). A P3 escalating at the retrieval/draft leg is flagged `mislabeled` ‚Äî it escalated (safe) but never exercised the faithfulness gate, so the gold retrieval was not actually strong ‚Äî distinct from a false-resolve, per the PRD failure indicator. `--include-p3` opt-in (needs `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`), so a scheduled/weekly artifact, never a per-PR block.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes *(pyflakes clean on all four touched eval files; mypy clean on `e7_runner.py`/`e7.py` modulo the shared `yaml`-stub note carried by `runner.py`/`e6.py`/`e7.py`; 24 `test_e7_runner` + 9 `test_e7` groups green.)*
**Validation Test:**
- **Setup:** A P3 question whose retrieved chunks are topically strong but contain no grounded answer, with a reference marking it should-escalate.
- **Steps:** 1. Run E7 over the P3 row. 2. Inspect the decision.
- **Expected Result:** Strong retrieval recorded, faithfulness gate fails, decision `escalate`; not counted as a false-resolve.
- **Failure Indicator:** P3 auto-resolved (a false-resolve) and uncaught, or the row escalating at the retrieval gate (mislabeled ‚Äî it must exercise the faithfulness gate).

### US-055: E7 metrics ‚Äî deflection / false-resolve / false-escalate
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done ‚Äî `evals/retrieval/e7_runner.py` (`compute_e7_metrics` + frozen `E7Metrics`/`ConsolidatedRate`/`PopulationContribution` value objects + `render_e7_metrics_section` + `e7_metrics` payload wiring) + `evals/retrieval/test_e7_runner.py` (4 new US-055 groups, 28 total); pyflakes clean, mypy-clean to the eval-package standard (2026-06-22).
**Description:** As an eval consumer, I want deflection rate, false-resolve rate, and false-escalate rate computed so that the operating objective (maximize deflection subject to false-resolve ‚â§ ceiling) is measurable.
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] The runner computes three rates: **deflection** = correctly auto-resolved / answerable (P2+P3 answerable subset, maximize); **false-resolve** = wrongly auto-resolved / unanswerable (the safety number); **false-escalate** = wrongly escalated / answerable (annoyance). *(`compute_e7_metrics(p1a, p2, p3)` consolidates the three per-leg results: **answerable** = the P2 population (the answerable subset of P2+P3 ‚Äî P3 has no faithful answer), so deflection = P2 auto-resolves / P2 and false-escalate = P2 false-escalates / P2; **unanswerable** = P1a (no context) + P3 (no faithful answer), so false-resolve = (P1a rows that cleared the gate, the retrieval-leg false-resolve) + (P3 auto-resolves, the faithfulness-leg false-resolve) / (P1a + P3). A P3 `mislabeled` row escalated safely so it stays in the unanswerable denominator but not the numerator. Computed in `amain` AFTER all legs run and emitted under `payload["e7_metrics"]`; the runner's exit code is still decided by the deterministic P1a invariant alone ‚Äî enforcing the ceiling is US-059.)*
- [x] Each rate carries its numerator/denominator and the population breakdown in the results JSON (so a regression is attributable to P1a/P2/P3). *(`ConsolidatedRate.to_dict()` emits `name`/`rate`/`numerator`/`denominator`/`safety`/`by_population`; `numerator`/`denominator` are derived as the sum of the per-population `PopulationContribution(population, numerator, denominator)` rows so the breakdown can never disagree with the headline. A rate over an empty population is `None` ‚Äî blind, never a false `0.0` ‚Äî so an opt-out P2/P3 leg cannot masquerade as a passing 0; P1a always runs, so the safety false-resolve number always carries at least its retrieval-leg contribution. A test hand-computes deflection 1/2 + false-escalate 1/2 + false-resolve 1/4 from a known one-wrong-resolve/one-wrong-escalate mix and asserts the false-resolve breakdown attributes to both P1a and P3.)*
- [x] false-resolve is flagged as the safety metric whose ceiling is a pinned invariant (consumed by US-059); deflection/false-escalate are tunable quality metrics. *(Only `false_resolve` carries `safety=True`; `deflection`/`false_escalate` carry `safety=False`. The render table marks false-resolve `üîí safety (pinned)` vs `tunable quality`; a test asserts the three `safety` flags. The number is structurally un-folded into any accuracy score ‚Äî it ships with its own n/d + breakdown for US-059 to gate `numerator/denominator ‚â§ ceiling`.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes *(pyflakes clean on `e7_runner.py`/`test_e7_runner.py`; mypy-clean modulo the shared `yaml`/`asyncpg` stubless-lib note carried by `runner.py`/`e6.py`/`e7.py`; 28 `test_e7_runner` groups green.)*
**Validation Test:**
- **Setup:** A small labeled set with a known mix of P1a/P2/P3 and a fixed knob setting producing one wrong auto-resolve and one wrong escalate.
- **Steps:** 1. Run the metrics computation. 2. Check the three rates against hand-computed values.
- **Expected Result:** Rates match the hand-computed numerator/denominator exactly; the false-resolve count includes the wrong auto-resolve.
- **Failure Indicator:** A false-resolve folded into a generic "accuracy" number, or rates that hide the denominator (cannot verify ‚â§ ceiling).

### US-056: E7 runner ‚Äî knob sweep, deflection-vs-false-resolve curve, knee
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done ‚Äî `evals/retrieval/e7_runner.py` (`run_e7_sweep` + frozen `E7Sweep`/`SweepPoint` + `_select_knee` + `render_e7_sweep_section` + `--sweep`/`--sweep-tau-sim`/`--sweep-n-min`/`--sweep-faithfulness-min`/`--false-resolve-ceiling` CLI + `e7_sweep` payload wiring + per-question memoizers) + `evals/retrieval/test_e7_runner.py` (5 new US-056 groups, 33 total); pyflakes clean, mypy-clean to the eval-package standard (2026-06-22).
**Description:** As an eval author, I want the runner to sweep œÑ_sim / N / faithfulness-cutoff and emit the deflection-vs-false-resolve curve so that the default operating point is the deflection-maximizing knee under the ceiling.
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] The runner sweeps a grid over the three knobs and, for each point, records (deflection, false-resolve, false-escalate); it emits the **deflection-vs-false-resolve curve** as structured data in the results JSON (and a summary-md table, like `render_summary` in `evals/retrieval/runner.py`). *(`run_e7_sweep` grids the Cartesian product `tau_sims √ó n_mins √ó faithfulness_mins` ‚Äî the E7 faithfulness knob is the offline 1-5 judge floor, NOT the runtime [0,1] `faithfulness_cutoff`, so the sweep is honest about which machinery it tunes. For each point it RE-RUNS the real US-052/053/054 legs + the US-055 `compute_e7_metrics` consolidation ‚Äî no rate logic is re-implemented. The result JSON (`payload["e7_sweep"]`) carries every grid point's full metrics (`points`), a sorted plottable `curve` of `(false_resolve, deflection, ‚Ä¶)`, and the knee; `render_e7_sweep_section` prints the curve table + the knee. The three knobs are pure POST-HOC thresholds on knob-independent raw materials ‚Äî œÑ_sim/N threshold the already-retrieved cosines (via the real `retrieval_gate`), the floor thresholds the already-scored 1-5 ‚Äî so retrieve/draft/judge are memoized per question and the whole grid costs the same LLM as ONE operating point; a test proves an 8-point grid drafts/judges each question ‚â§ once (4 calls, vs 24 un-memoized).)*
- [x] It selects the **knee** = the grid point maximizing deflection **subject to false-resolve ‚â§ ceiling**, and reports those knob values as the recommended config defaults (feeding US-050); if no point satisfies the ceiling it reports that explicitly rather than silently picking the least-bad. *(`_select_knee` filters to `false_resolve ‚â§ ceiling` (the buyer's `get_false_resolve_ceiling()`, US-050), then maximizes deflection, breaking ties toward lower false-resolve ‚Üí lower false-escalate ‚Üí lower grid index. `E7Sweep.recommended_config()` reports the knee's `ESCALATION_TAU_SIM`/`ESCALATION_N_MIN` directly (same machinery) plus the offline faithfulness floor as guidance (the runtime cutoff is a different [0,1] scale, tuned separately). When no point satisfies the ceiling, `knee=None` with `knee_reason="no_point_under_ceiling"` ‚Äî reported explicitly, NEVER downgraded to least-bad (a test asserts an all-infeasible grid yields this, not a chosen point); a separate `deflection_blind` reason covers a feasible-but-no-P2 grid. A 2√ó2√ó2 validation test pins the known knee (œÑ_sim=0.6, N_min=1, faith‚â•4 ‚Üí deflection 100%, false-resolve 0%) under a 0.05 ceiling and asserts equally-high-deflection points ABOVE the ceiling are rejected ‚Äî the objective is ceiling-constrained, not max-accuracy.)*
- [x] The sweep reuses the offline RAGAS/Claude faithfulness infra to score each point; it is structurally a scheduled (not per-PR) artifact because it is LLM-judged. *(The sweep wires the same OFFLINE cross-family Claude judge (`runner.judge_answer`, `JUDGE_MODEL=claude-haiku-4-5`) the P2/P3 legs use; `--sweep` is folded into the `include_judged` gate so it shares the `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` + `anthropic`-package requirement and lazy import ‚Äî LLM-judged ‚Üí scheduled/weekly (US-059), never a per-PR block. The deterministic P1a leg alone still decides this runner's exit code; the sweep only reports.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes *(pyflakes clean on `e7_runner.py`/`test_e7_runner.py`; mypy-clean modulo the shared `yaml`/`asyncpg` stubless-lib note carried by `runner.py`/`e6.py`/`e7.py`; 33 `test_e7_runner` groups green; CLI grid-range validation rejects out-of-range œÑ_sim/N/faith before any env read.)*
**Validation Test:**
- **Setup:** A labeled subset and a 2√ó2√ó2 knob grid with a known knee under a `false-resolve ‚â§ 0.05` ceiling.
- **Steps:** 1. Run the sweep. 2. Read the emitted curve and the chosen knee.
- **Expected Result:** The curve lists each grid point's (deflection, false-resolve); the knee is the highest-deflection point with false-resolve ‚â§ 0.05; knob values are reported.
- **Failure Indicator:** A knee with false-resolve above the ceiling chosen, no curve emitted, or "maximize accuracy" used instead of the ceiling-constrained objective.

### US-057: E7 P1b ‚Äî viewer-parameterized no-access population (reuse E4)
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done ‚Äî `evals/retrieval/e7_runner.py` (`run_e7_p1b` + `E7P1bResult`/`P1bDecision` + `RetrieveNoAccess` type + `render_e7_p1b_section` + `--include-p1b` CLI with the DB-backed no-access-replay closure + `e7_p1b` payload wiring + the P1b leak folded into `compute_e7_metrics` false-resolve, US-055) + `evals/retrieval/test_e7_runner.py` (7 new P1b groups, 40 total); pyflakes clean, mypy-clean modulo the shared `asyncpg` stub note (now carried like `runner.py`/`e6.py`). E2E-validated against the live local DB in keyword mode: every P2 question's gold retrieves 0 hits for the no-access viewer after ACL revocation ‚Üí weak gate ‚Üí escalate (2026-06-22).
**Description:** As an eval author, I want P1b generated by replaying P2 questions under a no-access viewer so that the access-filtered case is covered for free using the E4 viewer machinery, with no hand-authoring.
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] P1b rows are produced by running a P2 question under a no-access viewer via the existing `compute_visible_stable_ids(... "no_access" ...)` / `reset_viewer_acls` machinery in `evals/retrieval/runner.py` ‚Äî the *same question* is P2 for a full-access viewer and P1b for a no-access viewer. *(`run_e7_p1b` filters to the `answerable_faithful` (P2) rows and scores each via an injected `RetrieveNoAccess` callable. The `--include-p1b` CLI closure is the production wiring: per question it computes `r.compute_visible_stable_ids("no_access", q, all_sids, {})` = every stable id EXCEPT that question's gold, maps to chunk ids, calls `r.reset_viewer_acls(db_conn, {...})` to ACL-revoke the gold from the no-access viewer, then retrieves hybrid under the viewer's own JWT ‚Äî so the gold is filtered by RLS + the US-003 membership clause. `r.ensure_viewer_users` + `r.fetch_stable_id_map` set it up; no P1b gold is hand-authored. P1b needs DB write access so it requires `CORPUS_SEED_DATABASE_URL`/`DATABASE_URL` (guarded). E2E-proven against the live DB: the no-access viewer retrieves 0 of the gold for all 4 P2 questions.)*
- [x] From the no-access viewer's own retrieval, P1a and P1b are indistinguishable (filtered chunks invisible); the expected E7 decision for a P1b row is therefore the **same as P1a ‚Äî escalate** (caught at the retrieval gate, since the viewer's retrieval is weak). *(`run_e7_p1b` runs the SAME real `escalation.retrieval_gate` P1a uses over the (gold-filtered) no-access results; `P1bDecision` has `expected="escalate"` and the leg makes 0 draft / 0 judge calls ‚Äî structurally identical to P1a. A row that clears the gate is `correct=False` (the gold leaked to a no-access viewer ‚Äî an isolation/disclosure failure, worse than a P1a near-miss) and fails the run via the pinned exit-code, the same shape as a P1a cleared gate. The P1b leak also folds into the consolidated false-resolve number (`compute_e7_metrics(..., p1b)`, US-055) as its own attributable `P1b` population. Byte-equality of the customer-facing deferral is US-058.)*
- [x] **P1b detection (the privileged second pass) is absent from the code**, not merely default-OFF ‚Äî there is no unfiltered-second-pass code path; P1b rows trivially expect P1a output (US-058 asserts the equality). *(`run_e7_p1b` is given EXACTLY ONE retrieval callable ‚Äî the no-access one ‚Äî and never an owner/privileged retriever, so a "this is actually answerable for someone" signal structurally cannot reach the gate. A test asserts the leg retrieves exactly once per row (no second pass) and receives the full question dict (so the gold can be revoked), and the leg has no draft/judge path at all. The decision is derived solely from the no-access viewer's own filtered retrieval, exactly as P1a is.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes *(pyflakes clean on `e7_runner.py`/`test_e7_runner.py`; mypy-clean modulo the shared `yaml`/`asyncpg` stubless-lib note ‚Äî `e7_runner.py` now carries the `asyncpg` note like `runner.py`/`e6.py` since P1b needs DB access; the `ViewerKind` ACL-dict type resolves via a `TYPE_CHECKING`-only import so `runner` stays lazy-imported; 40 `test_e7_runner` groups green.)*
**Validation Test:**
- **Setup:** A P2 question with gold chunks, replayed under the no-access viewer (gold ACL-revoked).
- **Steps:** 1. Run the question as full-access ‚Üí P2. 2. Run it as no-access ‚Üí P1b. 3. Inspect both decisions.
- **Expected Result:** Full-access auto-resolves (P2); no-access escalates at the retrieval gate (P1b), with no privileged second pass invoked anywhere in the run.
- **Failure Indicator:** A privileged/unfiltered retrieval pass present in the code, or a P1b row resolving differently than P1a.

### US-058: E7 P1b non-disclosure assertion (pinned security invariant)
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done ‚Äî `evals/retrieval/e7_runner.py` (`assert_p1b_non_disclosure` + `E7P1bNonDisclosure`/`P1bLeak` + `_row_customer_output`/`_canonical_deferral_output` deriving the bytes through the REAL `escalation._escalated` constructor + `render_e7_p1b_non_disclosure_section` + `amain` wiring: computed when `--include-p1b` ran, emitted under `payload["e7_p1b_non_disclosure"]`, folded into the pinned exit code) + `evals/retrieval/test_e7_runner.py` (5 new US-058 groups, 45 total); pyflakes clean, mypy-clean to the eval-package standard (2026-06-22).
**Description:** As a security reviewer, I want an E7 assertion that the customer-facing P1b output is byte-for-byte identical to the P1a output so that escalating a no-access viewer never discloses that restricted content exists.
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] A pinned E7 assertion compares the **customer-facing output bytes** of every P1b row against the P1a generic deferral output and asserts exact equality (`assert p1b_customer_output == p1a_customer_output`, byte-for-byte) ‚Äî no `reason`, no `restricted-to`, no existence bit echoed to the customer. *(`assert_p1b_non_disclosure` derives each row's customer bytes by running the REAL production escalate constructor `escalation._escalated` ‚Üí `customer_message` (= `GENERIC_DEFERRAL`), fed each row's OWN per-row-DIFFERENT gate decision + internal `reason`, so the comparison proves the customer bytes are invariant to the differing internal reason/cosine/access state ‚Äî not a compare of two hardcoded copies. The reference is a real escalated P1a row's bytes; every P1b row must match. A test pins `p1a_reference == escalation.GENERIC_DEFERRAL` and that the P1a/P1b rows carried different `gate_reason`s.)*
- [x] The assertion is structured as a binary leak invariant (`assert leak == 0`), placed in the E8 **pinned `fail`** security/correctness class ‚Äî not buyer-downgradable to `comment`/`off`; silencing it requires deleting the eval, not configuring it down. *(`E7P1bNonDisclosure.passed` is `n_p1b > 0 and not leaks` ‚Äî any differing-bytes row OR a drafted (cleared-gate) row that would disclose a drafted answer is a `P1bLeak`; an empty population is structurally blind, NOT a pass (positive-control guard). In `amain` a non-pass sets the same `failed` flag the P1a/P1b gate invariants do ‚Äî there is no `comment`/`off` knob anywhere on the path.)*
- [x] The assertion is **deterministic** (string/byte equality on the deferral output, no LLM judge), so it can hard-block per-PR (US-059); access-aware reason/routing surfacing is explicitly out of scope (a future S4 authorized-agent surface, gated on its own existence-non-disclosure eval). *(Pure byte comparison ‚Äî no answerer/judge client touches this path; runs whenever `--include-p1b` is set (the deterministic per-PR tripwire, US-059). The injected-reason failure case (PRD validation step 4) is covered: a `p1b_output_fn` that appends `reason=access-denied` makes the assertion fail loudly with a `customer_bytes_differ` leak. No access-aware surfacing added.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes *(pyflakes clean on `e7_runner.py`/`test_e7_runner.py`; mypy introduces ZERO new errors ‚Äî only the shared pre-existing `escalation`/`retrieval`/`asyncpg` stubless-lib + sys.path-import notes carried by `runner.py`/`e6.py`/`e7.py` remain; 45 `test_e7_runner` groups green; `python -m evals.retrieval.e7_runner --help` wires end-to-end.)*
**Validation Test:**
- **Setup:** One P1a row and one P1b row (a P2 question under a no-access viewer) run through the customer-facing output path.
- **Steps:** 1. Capture the P1a customer output bytes. 2. Capture the P1b customer output bytes. 3. Run the assertion. 4. Inject a `reason=access-denied` into the P1b output and re-run.
- **Expected Result:** Bytes are identical and the assertion passes; the injected `reason` makes the assertion fail loudly (proving it actually pins the invariant).
- **Failure Indicator:** P1b output differing from P1a in any byte while the assertion still passes, or the assertion being configurable to `comment`/`off`.

### US-059: E7 CI placement ‚Äî per-PR deterministic tripwire vs scheduled sweep
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done ‚Äî per-PR tripwire wired into `.github/workflows/retrieval-eval.yml` (`e7_runner --include-p1b`, deterministic-only, reuses the seeded corpus + Supabase stack; `backend/escalation.py` added to the trigger paths) + new scheduled `.github/workflows/escalation-eval-weekly.yml` (full `--include-p1b --include-p2 --include-p3 --sweep`, publishes `docs/escalation-weekly/`, files/closes a deduped `e7-weekly-gate` issue, reflects the exit code). The false-resolve ceiling is now ENFORCED as a pinned safety invariant in the runner: `FalseResolveCeilingVerdict` + `assert_false_resolve_ceiling` + `render_e7_false_resolve_ceiling_section` + `amain` wiring (computed always, emitted under `payload["e7_false_resolve_ceiling"]`, folded into the exit code). CI placement + the F3/P5 detection-latency gap documented in `docs/evals.md` ¬ß6. `evals/retrieval/test_e7_runner.py` (5 new US-059 ceiling groups, 50 total); pyflakes clean, mypy-clean to the eval-package standard (2026-06-23).
**Description:** As a maintainer, I want the deterministic retrieval-gate behavior checked per-PR and the LLM-judge sweep run scheduled so that a judge wobble never red-bars an innocent merge while a retrieval-gate regression is caught immediately.
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] A **per-PR tripwire** runs the deterministic retrieval-gate decisions (pure arithmetic on cosine scores ‚Äî top-1 cosine `< œÑ_sim` / fewer than `N` cleared, no LLM) over a fixed labeled subset, plus the US-058 P1b non-disclosure byte-equality assertion; both may `fail` and block the merge (deterministic, like the retrieval recall floor in `.github/workflows/retrieval-eval.yml`). *(New "E7 escalation tripwire (PR, deterministic ‚Äî US-059)" step in `retrieval-eval.yml` runs `e7_runner --include-p1b` after the corpus seed, reusing this job's Supabase stack + env; NO `--include-p2/-p3/-sweep` and no `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`, so the path is pure cosine arithmetic + byte equality. The runner already pins P1a-cleared-gate, P1b-cleared-gate, and the non-disclosure byte mismatch into a non-zero exit AFTER writing the JSON ‚Äî exactly the E6 hard-gate shape. `backend/escalation.py` added to the workflow's `paths:` so a gate change re-runs it.)*
- [x] The **full E7 sweep with the LLM faithfulness judge** (P2/P3 scoring, the knob sweep + curve + knee) runs **scheduled/weekly** alongside the RAGAS weekly workflow (`.github/workflows/retrieval-eval-ragas-weekly.yml`, `cron`/`workflow_dispatch`); its `fail` = fail the scheduled workflow + file an issue, never block a merge. *(New `escalation-eval-weekly.yml`: `schedule` Sundays 06:00 UTC (staggered off the 02:00 nightly + 04:00 RAGAS) + `workflow_dispatch`, installs the full `requirements.txt` for `anthropic`, runs `e7_runner --include-p1b --include-p2 --include-p3 --sweep`, captures the exit code, publishes `docs/escalation-weekly/<DATE>.{json,md}`, files one deduped `e7-weekly-gate` issue on a red verdict + auto-closes stale ones on a green scheduled run, then "Reflect runner exit code" fails the scheduled workflow. It never gates a merge ‚Äî modeled on the weekly-RAGAS issue-filing flow.)*
- [x] The configurable E8 gate governs comment-vs-fail on a non-invariant E7 regression (deflection/false-escalate); the false-resolve ceiling breach fails like a safety invariant; the P1b assertion stays pinned `fail`. The accepted gap ‚Äî the faithfulness leg of false-resolve has up-to-a-week detection latency ‚Äî is documented (F3/P5), mitigated by the per-PR retrieval-leg tripwire. *(`assert_false_resolve_ceiling(metrics, get_false_resolve_ceiling())` folds a MEASURED consolidated false-resolve rate above the buyer's ceiling into the runner's `failed` exit flag ‚Äî pinned, never `comment`/`off` ‚Äî alongside the P1a/P1b gate + non-disclosure invariants; the deflection/false-escalate quality metrics stay tunable, deferred to the Area-F E8 gate (not yet built). The gate is structurally INERT per-PR (its only per-PR contributor is the retrieval leg, already pinned), so the faithfulness-leg false-resolve is only scored weekly ‚Äî the up-to-a-week detection-latency gap is documented as the ADR-0003 F3/P5 line in `docs/evals.md` ¬ß6, mitigated by the per-PR retrieval-leg tripwire.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes *(pyflakes clean on `e7_runner.py`/`test_e7_runner.py`; mypy adds ZERO new errors ‚Äî `MYPYPATH=backend mypy ‚Ä¶ e7_runner.py` ‚Üí "no issues found"; only the shared pre-existing stubless-lib/sys.path notes carried by `runner.py`/`e6.py` remain. 50 `test_e7_runner` groups green; both workflow YAMLs parse + every `run:` block passes `bash -n`; `e7_runner --help` wires end-to-end.)*
**Validation Test:**
- **Setup:** A PR that loosens the retrieval gate so a P1a row drafts (a retrieval-leg false-resolve), and separately a PR that only perturbs a faithfulness score.
- **Steps:** 1. Run the per-PR tripwire on the gate-loosening PR. 2. Run it on the faithfulness-only PR. 3. Confirm the weekly workflow runs the full sweep.
- **Expected Result:** The gate-loosening PR fails the per-PR tripwire (blocks merge); the faithfulness-only PR passes per-PR (caught later by the scheduled sweep); the weekly workflow runs the judge sweep + curve.
- **Failure Indicator:** An LLM judge call on the per-PR path (flaky merge gating), the P1b assertion only running weekly, or a per-PR `fail` offered for the judge-driven deflection metric.

#### Functional requirements (this area)
- FR-S1: The support face decides answer-vs-escalate via a deterministic deflection pipeline (`retrieve once ‚Üí retrieval gate ‚Üí [if strong] draft ‚Üí faithfulness gate ‚Üí answer-or-escalate`); the decision is control flow, never a model `escalate()` tool, and never the M1 agentic loop.
- FR-S2: The escalation signal is retrieval-grounded OR faithfulness-grounded, run as an OR-short-circuit cascade: the retrieval gate fires first (escalate with no draft, no judge call); only strong-retrieval queries draft + run the faithfulness gate.
- FR-S3: The retrieval gate is cosine-defined on raw `cosine_similarity ‚àà [0,1]` (top-1 `< œÑ_sim` OR fewer than `N` clear `match_threshold`), never the RRF fused score; `retrieval.py` surfaces the pre-fusion cosine through fusion; the gate is reranker-optional.
- FR-S4: The runtime faithfulness gate is exactly one structured-output judge call `{supported, score}` on a cheap model, fail-closed, net-new code distinct from the offline RAGAS metric.
- FR-S5: œÑ_sim / N / faithfulness-cutoff are global typed config (defaults from the E7 knee); the false-resolve ceiling is the single buyer-set risk number; per-workspace tuning is deferred but config-shaped.
- FR-S6: E7 is a three-population golden set (P1a/P1b, P2, P3) scored by the offline RAGAS + cross-family judge infra; it computes deflection / false-resolve / false-escalate, sweeps the knobs, emits the deflection-vs-false-resolve curve, and picks the knee under the ceiling.
- FR-S7: Customer-facing P1b output is byte-for-byte identical to P1a (pinned, deterministic non-disclosure assertion); P1b detection / the privileged second pass is absent from v1 code.
- FR-S8: The deterministic retrieval-gate tripwire + the P1b non-disclosure assertion run per-PR and may block merge; the LLM-judge deflection/false-resolve sweep runs scheduled (weekly) and files an issue on regression rather than blocking.

#### Non-goals (this area)
- A standalone classifier escalation signal (PRD option 2) ‚Äî cloneable, un-grounded; rejected in favor of the 3+4 retrieval+faithfulness cascade.
- A model-discretion `escalate()` tool ‚Äî un-evalable, re-introduces Risk #3 overconfidence, cloneable; the decision stays deterministic control flow.
- Reusing the M1 agentic tool loop for the support face ‚Äî the model has usually drafted by loop termination, destroying the OR short-circuit.
- Thresholding the RRF fused score for "weak retrieval" ‚Äî RRF is a rank artifact, not comparable across queries.
- Full RAGAS claim-decomposition at runtime ‚Äî several calls, fatal in the latency path; the runtime gate is one call.
- P1b detection / the privileged unfiltered second pass ‚Äî absent from v1, not merely default-OFF; access-aware routing is a documented future capability gated on a content-blind-for-all design + its own existence-non-disclosure eval, never opened for the bot alone.
- Showing the customer a `reason=access-denied` / any existence bit on escalation ‚Äî the access-aware reason is surfaced only to an authorized agent on the S4 handoff surface (out of scope here).
- Per-workspace knob tuning ‚Äî deferred (config-shaped, no schema migration in v1).
- The user-initiated "talk to a human" widget button ‚Äî owned by the support-surface section; referenced, not built here.
- A per-PR LLM-judged false-resolve check ‚Äî the faithfulness leg is scheduled/weekly (accepted up-to-a-week detection latency); only the deterministic retrieval-leg tripwire blocks merge.
## E. Support surface ‚Äî widget runtime + conversation/handoff (ADR-0008 + ADR-0004)

This section builds the anonymous embeddable support widget (S3) and the conversation-state + human-handoff model (S4) as one coherent runtime. It **consumes the workspace layer (ADR-0002)** ‚Äî every new resource is gated by the *same* `viewer ‚àà members(workspace_id)` membership clause and the active-workspace resolution rules (default-when-sole / 400-on-ambiguous), and the support bot is a `role='member'` `workspace_membership` principal ‚Äî and it **consumes the escalation pipeline (ADR-0003)**: the per-turn answer-vs-escalate decision (retrieval gate ‚Üí optional draft ‚Üí faithfulness gate) is reused wholesale; this section only adds the *conversation-level latch* over it, the runtime that runs it for an anonymous customer, and the read-back channel that returns a human reply. The widget is a cross-origin iframe served from the kit's own origin plus a tiny loader `<script>` (max-isolation embed); the backend self-signs short-lived Supabase-compatible JWTs (one minting primitive) for the **bot** (server-side only) while the **customer** holds only an opaque per-conversation token and is structurally off the Supabase JWT/Realtime trust surface. S5 teams/assignment routing and P1b access-aware detection are explicitly out of scope. Stories below assume the ADR-0002 workspace section landed `workspace_membership(user_id, workspace_id, role)` and the membership clause inside `match_chunks` *before* this section's migrations run.

### US-066: `conversations` + `conversation_messages` migration with membership RLS
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done ‚Äî `supabase/migrations/20260623120000_init_conversations.sql` adds the `conversations` + `conversation_messages` pair with the ADR-0002 membership `EXISTS` clause on every policy (`role` in no predicate), child message policies delegating to the parent conversation's workspace (mirroring `messages`‚Üí`threads` in `20260416120000_init_threads_messages.sql`), the `(workspace_id, status)` + `(conversation_id, created_at asc)` indexes, and `threads`/`messages` left untouched. `bot_user_id`/`claimed_by` FKs are `ON DELETE SET NULL` (review refinement, mirroring the `documents.workspace_id` no-cascade precedent); `conversation_messages.conversation_id` cascades. Cross-workspace zero-leak pinned by `backend/test_us066_conversations_rls.py` (run via `python -m backend.test_us066_conversations_rls` against a local Supabase with `DATABASE_URL` set) ‚Äî `== 0` leak asserts + same-workspace positive control + a structural check that no policy references `wm.role`. The two-trust-models invariant is also recorded in `AGENTS.md`.
**Description:** As the platform, I want a new `conversations` + `conversation_messages` table pair (NOT an extension of `threads`) so that support conversations have workspace-membership RLS without branching the leak-proof `threads`/`messages` predicate on a `kind` discriminator (ADR-0004, PRD Risk #3).
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] New migration creates `conversations(id uuid pk, workspace_id uuid NOT NULL references workspaces, bot_user_id uuid references auth.users, customer_email text NULL, status text NOT NULL default 'active', escalated_at timestamptz NULL, channel text NOT NULL default 'widget', claimed_by uuid NULL references auth.users, claimed_at timestamptz NULL, created_at timestamptz NOT NULL default now())` per ADR-0004 + CONTEXT (claimed_by/claimed_at added by ADR-0008). *(`bot_user_id`/`claimed_by` carry `ON DELETE SET NULL` per the review refinement.)*
- [x] `conversation_messages` mirrors `messages` shape: `(id, conversation_id references conversations on delete cascade, role check in ('user','assistant','system','tool'), content text, tool_calls jsonb NULL, tool_call_id text NULL, name text NULL, created_at)` ‚Äî `tool_calls` kept for schema parity, null/unused for widget convos.
- [x] RLS enabled on both; `conversations` SELECT/UPDATE policy = `EXISTS (select 1 from workspace_membership wm where wm.workspace_id = conversations.workspace_id and wm.user_id = auth.uid())` ‚Äî the SAME ADR-0002 clause; `role` appears in NO predicate. `conversation_messages` policies delegate to the parent conversation's membership (mirrors `messages`‚Üí`threads` in `20260416120000_init_threads_messages.sql`). *(Matching membership-gated INSERT/DELETE policies are added on both tables for parity with the threads/messages precedent.)*
- [x] `threads`/`messages` tables and their owner-only policies are untouched.
- [x] Index on `conversations(workspace_id, status)` (queue lists escalated per workspace) and `conversation_messages(conversation_id, created_at asc)`.
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes and migration applies.
**Validation Test:**
- **Setup:** Apply migration. Seed two workspaces W1, W2; user U1 ‚àà W1 only. Insert a conversation C1 in W1, C2 in W2.
- **Steps:** 1. As U1 (real JWT) `GET /rest/v1/conversations`. 2. Attempt to read C2 directly by id.
- **Expected Result:** C1 returned; C2 returns 0 rows (RLS-hidden, indistinguishable from not-found).
- **Failure Indicator:** U1 can read C2, or any `conversations` policy references `wm.role`.

### US-067: Conversation status machine + escalation latch + derivable deflection
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done (shipped via PR #29) - `supabase/migrations/20260623130000_conversation_status_machine.sql` installs the one-way status latch at the DB level: an idempotently-added CHECK `status in ('active','escalated','resolved')` plus the `create or replace` BEFORE INSERT OR UPDATE trigger `_conversations_status_guard` (`conversations_status_guard`) that rejects `escalated -> active` and any `resolved -> *` (resolved is terminal; `resolved -> resolved` no-op allowed) and OWNS `escalated_at` on BOTH the INSERT and UPDATE paths - callers never set it: a row born `escalated` is latched `now()`, any other birth status (incl. `resolved`) gets a null latch, the first transition into `escalated` stamps `now()`, and every later write preserves it verbatim. Deflection is therefore derivable (`resolved AND escalated_at IS NULL` = deflected; `IS NOT NULL` = human-handled) with no `resolved_by_*` flag; the divide-by-zero-guarded SQL is documented in `AGENTS.md` + the migration header. Test: `python -m backend.test_conversation_status_machine` (DB-level via asyncpg as `postgres`, skips cleanly when the local DB / `conversations` table is absent). NOTE: this story ships ONLY the DB latch; the runtime "first escalating turn stops the ADR-0003 bot pipeline" behaviour (criterion 3) is wired + asserted in US-080, so that one box stays unchecked here.
**Description:** As the platform, I want `active ‚Üí escalated ‚Üí resolved` enforced as a one-way latch with `escalated_at` set exactly once so that deflection is derivable (`resolved AND escalated_at IS NULL` = deflected; `IS NOT NULL` = human-handled) without a `resolved_by_bot`/`resolved_by_human` state explosion (ADR-0004).
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] DB CHECK constraint `status in ('active','escalated','resolved')`; a transition guard (trigger or service-layer assertion) rejects `escalated ‚Üí active` and `resolved ‚Üí *` (resolved is terminal). *(CHECK constraint + the `_conversations_status_guard` BEFORE INSERT/UPDATE trigger reject `escalated -> active` and `resolved -> *`; the status-machine test exercises both rejections.)*
- [x] `escalated_at` is set on the *first* escalate transition and is never cleared on later writes (latch); set-once enforced (trigger refuses to overwrite a non-null `escalated_at`). *(Trigger owns `escalated_at` set-once on both INSERT and UPDATE; the test asserts it stays `t0` across a second escalate write.)*
- [x] First escalating turn latches the whole conversation: after latch the bot never runs the ADR-0003 pipeline again for that conversation (asserted in US-080). *(Delivered + asserted in US-080: `widget_conversation_message` short-circuits an already-`escalated` conversation to `conversation`+`done` without invoking `_run_widget_bot_turn`; `backend/test_us080_escalation_latch.py` pins the pipeline-entry counter staying flat across later messages. The DB latch enabling it was delivered by this story.)*
- [x] A documented SQL snippet computes deflection rate from production data: `count(*) filter (where status='resolved' and escalated_at is null) / count(*) filter (where status='resolved')`. *(Divide-by-zero-guarded deflection SQL documented in `AGENTS.md` and the migration header.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes and migration applies. *(no-mistakes pipeline green; PR #29 merged into `main`; the status-machine test applies the migration against the live local DB.)*
**Validation Test:**
- **Setup:** Conversation C in `active`.
- **Steps:** 1. Transition to `escalated`, record `escalated_at = t0`. 2. Attempt a second escalate write (should not move `escalated_at`). 3. Attempt `escalated ‚Üí active`. 4. Transition to `resolved`; attempt `resolved ‚Üí escalated`.
- **Expected Result:** `escalated_at` stays `t0`; step 3 rejected; step 4 second transition rejected (terminal).
- **Failure Indicator:** `escalated_at` changes after first set, or any backward/out-of-terminal transition succeeds.

### US-068: Self-signed Supabase-compatible JWT minting primitive (server-side)
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done ‚Äî `backend/supabase_jwt.py:mint_supabase_jwt(sub, ttl_seconds, *, secret=None)` self-signs a short-lived HS256 JWT with `SUPABASE_JWT_SECRET` (resolved fail-closed at call time so a knowledge-assistant-only deploy need not set it; `secret` is a test-only override) carrying exactly `sub`/`role='authenticated'`/`aud='authenticated'`/`iat`/`exp=iat+ttl`, validating `ttl_seconds > 0` (and rejecting `bool`/non-int). The module docstring records the ADR-0008 rationale (self-sign over a per-request GoTrue admin-API session: no round-trip, service-role key stays out of the hot path) and the P5 threat-model line (NEW signing surface; server-side only; never client-facing). `main.py` documents the NEW optional `SUPABASE_JWT_SECRET` env without gating startup on it; PyJWT promoted to a direct pin in `requirements.txt`. The two-trust-models/JWT-minting invariants are recorded in `AGENTS.md`. Test: `python -m backend.test_supabase_jwt` ‚Äî 8 unit assertions (always run, no DB/secrets) + 3 integration assertions against local Supabase (a minted token is accepted by PostgREST and resolves `auth.uid()` to `sub`; a token for a different `sub` reads 0 rows; an expired token is rejected with PGRST303), skipping cleanly when the DB/`conversations` table is absent.
**Description:** As the backend, I want one minting primitive that self-signs short-lived HS256 Supabase-compatible JWTs with the **project JWT secret** so that the bot's `sub=bot_user_id` token is an ordinary `role=authenticated` JWT that `auth.uid()` + RLS resolve natively ‚Äî a new *issuer* beside GoTrue, no new enforcement path (ADR-0008).
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] A `mint_supabase_jwt(sub, ttl_seconds)` helper signs HS256 with `SUPABASE_JWT_SECRET` (NEW env, documented as a P5 threat-model line ‚Äî backend now holds the signing secret, previously only the anon key); claims include `sub`, `role='authenticated'`, `aud='authenticated'`, `exp`, `iat`.
- [x] Used ONLY server-side for the bot token (~60s); the function is never exposed over any endpoint and its output never reaches an HTTP response body sent to the iframe. *(No endpoint imports it; `main.py` only documents the env. Server-side-only invariant stated in the module docstring + AGENTS.md; the no-leak-to-SSE/response/log enforcement is wired at the call site in US-070.)*
- [x] A token minted by this helper is accepted by PostgREST/`match_chunks` exactly like a GoTrue-issued JWT (resolves `auth.uid()` to `sub`). *(Integration test proves PostgREST acceptance + `auth.uid()==sub` via the same membership-RLS path the bot token traverses; a token for a different `sub` reads 0 rows.)*
- [x] Chosen over a GoTrue admin-API session per request (avoids round-trip + service-role key in the request path) ‚Äî recorded in code comment referencing ADR-0008.
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes. *(mypy clean on `supabase_jwt.py`; the test's only mypy note is the pre-existing `asyncpg` missing-stubs one shared by every DB test.)*
**Validation Test:**
- **Setup:** Configure `SUPABASE_JWT_SECRET` to the project secret. Have a known `auth.users` id `B`.
- **Steps:** 1. `mint_supabase_jwt(sub=B, ttl=60)`. 2. Call `GET /rest/v1/...` or RPC `match_chunks` with that token. 3. Wait past TTL, retry.
- **Expected Result:** Step 2 resolves `auth.uid() == B`; step 3 rejected (expired).
- **Failure Indicator:** A minted token is rejected by PostgREST when fresh, or accepted after `exp`, or appears in any client-facing payload.

### US-069: Lazy support-bot provisioning + `is_bot` flag (one bot per workspace)
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done (shipped via PR #32) - `supabase/migrations/20260624120000_workspace_membership_is_bot.sql` adds `is_bot boolean not null default false` to `workspace_membership` (a FLAG, not a role - it enters NO retrieval predicate; ADR-0002 intact) plus the partial unique index `workspace_membership_one_bot_per_workspace ... where is_bot` that hard-guarantees exactly one bot per workspace even under two concurrent first-time provisions (the loser takes a unique violation). `backend/support_bot.py:provision_workspace_bot(workspace_id)` is the SINGLE, lazy, idempotent provisioning path: it creates the bot `auth.users` row + a `workspace_membership(role='member', is_bot=true)` row under the service-role key (resolved fail-closed when unset), returns the `bot_user_id`, and nothing provisions a bot at workspace-creation time. The bot is `role='member'` (administrative role grants no content access, so it reads only share-to-bot docs via `chunk_acl`; NO dedicated bot content-role exists anywhere), and member-management listings filter `where is_bot = false`. Test: `python -m backend.test_us069_bot_provisioning`. Downstream wiring of this primitive: the first-key-issuance trigger is US-072 and the `conversations.bot_user_id` assignment is US-078.
**Description:** As an admin enabling support, I want the per-workspace support bot (`auth.users` row + `workspace_membership` with `role='member'`, `is_bot=true`) created lazily on first widget-key issuance so that a knowledge-assistant-only deployment never spawns a bot and no new content role is added (ADR-0008; ADR-0002 intact).
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] Migration adds `is_bot boolean NOT NULL default false` to `workspace_membership` (a flag, not a role ‚Äî changes no retrieval predicate; ADR-0002 untouched). *(`add column if not exists is_bot boolean not null default false`; the migration header states `is_bot` enters no predicate - a flag, like `role`.)*
- [x] Provisioning (service-role/admin API) creates the bot `auth.users` row + a `workspace_membership(role='member', is_bot=true)` row, runs **lazily** when support is first enabled (first key issued), idempotently ‚Äî exactly **one bot per workspace**, not per key; `conversations.bot_user_id` is set from it. *(`provision_workspace_bot` creates the `auth.users` row + the `is_bot=true, role='member'` membership lazily/idempotently; one-per-workspace is hard-enforced by the partial unique index. The "first key issued" caller is US-072 and the `conversations.bot_user_id` assignment is US-078.)*
- [x] Bot membership is excluded from member-management UI listings and is available for an optional explicit write-deny policy. *(Member-management listings filter `where is_bot = false`; the migration header documents the optional explicit write-deny hook.)*
- [x] Bot is `role='member'` ‚Äî administrative-only role grants no content access, so the bot sees only documents granted via share-to-bot through `chunk_acl`; NO dedicated `bot` content-role exists anywhere. *(Provisioned `role='member'`; no `bot` content-role anywhere - the `is_bot` flag changes no boundary, so the bot sees only share-to-bot `chunk_acl` grants.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes and migration applies. *(no-mistakes pipeline green; PR #32 merged into `main`; `test_us069_bot_provisioning` green.)*
**Validation Test:**
- **Setup:** Workspace W with no support enabled (no bot row).
- **Steps:** 1. Issue first widget key for W (US-072). 2. Issue a second key for W. 3. Inspect `workspace_membership` for W.
- **Expected Result:** Exactly one `is_bot=true` member row exists after both keys; `role='member'`; second key issuance does NOT create a second bot.
- **Failure Indicator:** Two bot rows, a bot with `role='admin'`, or a bot created at workspace creation before any key.

### US-070: Support-bot retrieval ‚Äî per-turn bot token calls `match_chunks` as the bot
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done (shipped via PR #33) - the retrieval half of `backend/support_bot.py` runs the deflection pipeline AS the bot: per customer turn it mints a ~60s Supabase JWT (`sub = bot_user_id`, via US-068's `mint_supabase_jwt`), calls the existing `match_chunks` / `keyword_search` RPCs with it, then discards it - no token is cached across turns (two turns produce two distinct mints). No new retrieval predicate and NO `principal_ids` from the backend: the DB resolves the bot's principal set from `auth.uid()`, so the US-003 owner-OR-ACL + `workspace_membership` boundary applies wholesale and the bot answers only from share-to-bot documents. The conversation's `workspace_id` is passed as the ORDINARY non-security `filter_workspace_id` narrowing param added by `20260624150000_match_chunks_workspace_filter.sql` / `20260624150100_keyword_search_workspace_filter.sql` (AND-ed like `filter_topics`; can only narrow within what `auth.uid()` already sees, never widen - explicitly distinct from the trust boundary). The bot token never reaches the returned `DeflectionResult`, any SSE/response body, or a propagated retrieval error. Tests: `python -m backend.test_us070_bot_retrieval` (unit, injected minter) + `backend/test_us070_bot_retrieval_integration.py`.
**Description:** As the deflection pipeline, I want each customer turn to mint a ~60s bot token and call `match_chunks` as `bot_user_id` so that retrieval reuses the `auth.uid()` membership + owner-OR-ACL boundary wholesale and the bot answers only from share-to-bot documents (CONTEXT Support-bot principal; ADR-0008).
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] Per turn: mint bot token (US-068), call existing `match_chunks` RPC with that token, discard the token after the call ‚Äî no caching of bot tokens across turns. *(Per-turn mint via the injected minter ‚Üí `match_chunks`/`keyword_search` ‚Üí discard; the unit test proves exactly one mint per turn and two turns -> two distinct tokens, no caching.)*
- [x] No new retrieval predicate, no `principal_ids` passed from the backend ‚Äî the DB resolves the bot's principal set from `auth.uid()` (CONTEXT principal-set resolution). *(No new predicate and no `principal_ids` passed; the migration header states the boundary stays the US-003 owner-OR-ACL + membership clause resolved from `auth.uid()`.)*
- [x] The bot token is NEVER written to any SSE event, response body, or log line that reaches the client. *(Token absent from the `DeflectionResult`, any SSE/response body, and a propagated retrieval error - asserted by the unit test.)*
