- [x] Active-workspace filter passed as the ordinary non-security `match_chunks` param (resolved from the conversation's `workspace_id`), distinct from the trust boundary. *(Conversation `workspace_id` passed as the ordinary `filter_workspace_id`; AND-ed narrowing that can only under-return within `auth.uid()`'s visibility, never widen.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes. *(no-mistakes pipeline green; PR #33 merged into `main`.)*
**Validation Test:**
- **Setup:** Workspace W with doc D shared-to-bot and doc E NOT shared-to-bot. Provision bot B.
- **Steps:** 1. Run a turn whose answer lives in D ‚Üí inspect retrieved chunk ids. 2. Run a turn whose answer lives only in E.
- **Expected Result:** Step 1 retrieves D's chunks; step 2 retrieves 0 chunks from E (bot has no grant). Bot token absent from all client-visible output.
- **Failure Indicator:** Bot retrieves E's chunks, or a bot token leaks into an SSE/response/log surface.

### US-071: Opaque per-conversation customer token ‚Äî issuance, hashed storage, resume
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done (shipped via PR #34) - the opaque per-conversation customer token is a THIRD trust boundary (backend-mediated only) beside owner-only `threads/messages` and workspace-membership `conversations`. `backend/conversation_tokens.py` holds the pure primitives: `generate_conversation_token()` = 256-bit `secrets.token_urlsafe(32)` (opaque, non-JWT, signed with nothing - deliberately NOT US-068's `mint_supabase_jwt`); `hash_conversation_token()` = SHA-256 hex, the ONLY stored representation; `CONVERSATION_TOKEN_TTL_SECONDS = 24h` is the issuance TTL. Migration `supabase/migrations/20260624160000_conversation_tokens.sql` adds `conversation_tokens(token_hash pk, conversation_id fk ON DELETE CASCADE, expires_at, created_at)` with **RLS enabled and ZERO policies** (anon/authenticated denied wholesale), plus the `resume_conversation(p_token_hash text, p_slide boolean default true)` SECURITY DEFINER RPC - the single authoritative read path - revoked from `public, anon, authenticated` by name then granted to `service_role` ONLY (Supabase default-privileges gotcha; `has_function_privilege('anon', ...)` = false). The customer presents the raw token over HTTP via the `X-Conversation-Token` header (deliberately not `Authorization`); `main.py` hashes it and calls the RPC as the service role through `_require_service_role_headers()` (fail-closed 503 when `SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY` unset). `POST /widget/conversations/resume` slides the 24h window; `GET /widget/conversations/{id}/transcript` passes `slide=False` (a safe/idempotent read never extends the token) and enforces the X/Y binding (resumed id must equal path id). Invalidated on resolve twice over: the RPC's `status <> 'resolved'` gate + the AFTER-UPDATE `conversations_purge_tokens_on_resolve` trigger that deletes the conversation's token rows. No server-side customer-identity table; `workspace_membership.role` appears nowhere (ADR-0002 intact). `_issue_conversation_token()` is the issuance helper US-078 calls on first message; public-widget CORS stays US-074's concern (no widening of `/api/*` `FRONTEND_ORIGINS`). Test: `python -m backend.test_us071_conversation_tokens` - a unit layer (always runs: opaque/unique/URL-safe/not-JWT-shaped token, one-way 64-hex hash != raw, 24h TTL) + an integration/security layer (skips cleanly without local Supabase - both the asyncpg connect and the PostgREST httpx calls are guarded; `_assert_schema` verifies RLS-on + 0 policies + service_role-only grant + purge trigger) encoding the PRD validation test (resume(Tx)=X only, Tx can never resolve to Y, anon cannot call the RPC while service-role can, expiry/refresh + slide=False behave, resolving X purges Tx and rejects its resume).
**Description:** As an anonymous customer, I want an opaque random backend-issued token (NOT a Supabase JWT) bound to one `conversation_id`, stored hashed, with lifetime tracking the conversation so that I can reconnect across reloads while staying structurally off the Supabase trust surface (ADR-0008; amends ADR-0004).
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] Token is cryptographically-random opaque bytes, NOT signed with the JWT secret; only its hash is stored (e.g. `conversation_tokens(token_hash, conversation_id, expires_at, created_at)` or a hashed column on `conversations`); raw token returned once at conversation creation, only to the iframe. *(`conversation_tokens.py`: 256-bit `secrets.token_urlsafe(32)`, SHA-256 hex the only persisted form; dedicated `conversation_tokens(token_hash pk, conversation_id fk, expires_at, created_at)` table; `_issue_conversation_token` returns the raw token once for US-078's first-message flow and it never reaches a log/SSE/response body.)*
- [x] Lifetime ‚âà24h, refreshed on activity while `status != resolved`, invalidated on resolve; bound to exactly one `conversation_id`. *(`CONVERSATION_TOKEN_TTL_SECONDS=24h`; RPC slides `expires_at = now() + interval '24 hours'` when `p_slide` true; FK binds exactly one conversation; invalidated twice over - the RPC's `status <> 'resolved'` gate + the `conversations_purge_tokens_on_resolve` AFTER-UPDATE trigger that deletes the rows.)*
- [x] A resume/revalidate endpoint accepts the opaque token, checks `not expired AND status != resolved`, and on success returns the conversation + allows SSE reconnect + transcript `GET`; no/expired/resolved ‚Üí caller starts a fresh conversation on next first-message. *(`POST /widget/conversations/resume` + `GET /widget/conversations/{id}/transcript`, authed by the `X-Conversation-Token` header ‚Üí `resume_conversation` RPC; transcript enforces the X/Y binding (resumed id == path id) with `slide=False`; a miss returns None so the caller starts fresh. The customer SSE endpoint that consumes this authorization is wired later, US-080.)*
- [x] There is NO server-side customer-identity table ‚Äî continuity comes only from the iframe-origin-stored token. *(Only `conversation_tokens` (hashes) exists - no customer/session/identity table; `workspace_membership.role` referenced nowhere.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes and migration applies. *(no-mistakes pipeline green - review/test/lint passed, PR #34 squash-merged into `main`; `_assert_schema` confirms the migration applies with RLS on, 0 policies, service_role-only grant, and the purge trigger present.)*
**Validation Test (security-critical):**
- **Setup:** Conversation X (token Tx) and conversation Y (token Ty), different workspaces.
- **Steps:** 1. Call transcript/resume with Tx for X. 2. Call transcript/resume with Tx requesting Y's id. 3. Resolve X, then resume with Tx.
- **Expected Result:** Step 1 returns X only; step 2 returns **0 rows / rejected** (token bound to X, cannot read Y); step 3 rejected (invalidated on resolve).
- **Failure Indicator:** Tx reads Y or any conversation other than X, or a resolved conversation's token still resumes.

### US-072: `widget_keys` table + key resolution (validate-not-revoked before minting)
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done (merged to `main` via PR #35, squash commit `943b527`) - `supabase/migrations/20260624130000_widget_keys.sql` adds the `widget_keys` registry (exact PRD columns; `public_key` non-secret + globally `unique`, `allowed_origins text[] not null default '{}'` for US-073, `revoked_at` NULL = active, `created_by` FK `ON DELETE SET NULL`) with RLS enabled and admin-only `SELECT`/`INSERT`/`UPDATE` policies gated on the ADR-0002 membership clause WITH `role='admin'` - the ONE legitimate place `role` enters a predicate (key management IS the administrative action); NO `DELETE` policy (rotate = revoke, retained for audit). The migration also installs a `BEFORE UPDATE` trigger (`widget_keys_revoke_guard`) that makes revocation a true one-way **DB latch** - a non-null `revoked_at` can never be cleared or changed, matching the US-067 "enforced in the DB, not just the service layer" precedent (a direct PostgREST PATCH clearing `revoked_at` is rejected, not merely avoided by the endpoint). `backend/widget_keys.py` holds the pure key primitives (`generate_public_key` ‚Üí `wk_pk_<urlsafe>`, non-secret; `is_widget_public_key` shape guard); `main.py` adds the admin-authed management endpoints (`POST`/`GET /api/support/widget-keys`, `POST /api/support/widget-keys/{id}/revoke` - all INSERT/SELECT/UPDATE under the admin's own JWT so the admin RLS IS the authorization, with upstream PostgREST `5xx ‚Üí 502` / malformed-id `‚Üí 400` mapping consistent across all four endpoints) and the anonymous `POST /widget/keys/resolve` (reuses `_require_service_role_headers()`, gates on `revoked_at IS NULL`, leaks no workspace topology). Resolution is the not-revoked gate: a revoked/unknown key resolves to ZERO rows and mints nothing; the opaque per-conversation token (US-071) is independent of the key once minted, so revoking never kills a live conversation. First-key bot provisioning is **live**: `_ensure_workspace_bot` is the single, idempotent, best-effort call site for US-069's `provision_workspace_bot(workspace_id, http=...)` (US-069 is on `main`; provisioning is best-effort so a failure never blocks key issuance, and US-069 also provisions lazily at first conversation, US-078). Tests: `python -m backend.test_us072_widget_keys` (unit primitives + a DB/RLS security layer: revoked-key-mints-nothing, admin-only reads/writes, live-conversation-survives-revocation, and the revoke-latch un-revoke rejection). Shipped through the no-mistakes gate (review + tests + green CI); the gate found and the pipeline fixed three things the first cut missed - DRY reuse of `_require_service_role_headers()` (the helper only existed after the rebase onto `main`), the `5xx ‚Üí 502` upstream-error mapping across all four endpoints, and the DB revoke latch.
**Description:** As the widget runtime, I want `widget_keys` storing a non-secret public key per workspace and a resolution endpoint that validates not-revoked before any minting so that a public key resolves to `(workspace_id, bot_user_id)` and a revoked key cannot start new conversations (ADR-0008; CONTEXT widget-key mechanics).
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] Migration creates `widget_keys(id, workspace_id, public_key text unique, label text, allowed_origins text[], revoked_at timestamptz NULL, created_by uuid, created_at)`; public_key is non-secret (embedded in client JS). *(`20260624130000_widget_keys.sql` - exact columns; `public_key` non-secret + `unique`, the `wk_pk_` prefix makes its role self-evident in client JS; migration applies clean against the live local DB.)*
- [x] Multiple keys per workspace allowed; rotate = issue-new + revoke-old (no auto-rotation). *(No per-workspace unique constraint - any number of keys per workspace; `POST /api/support/widget-keys` issues, `POST .../{id}/revoke` flips `revoked_at` one-way - enforced as a true DB latch by the `widget_keys_revoke_guard` trigger (a non-null `revoked_at` can never be cleared/changed); no auto-rotation anywhere.)*
- [x] Resolution validates `revoked_at IS NULL` before minting/creating anything; **revoking blocks NEW conversations but never terminates live ones** (the opaque per-conversation token is independent of the key once minted). *(`_resolve_widget_key` / `POST /widget/keys/resolve` gate on `revoked_at=is.null` - a revoked key returns 0 rows ‚Üí 404, no minting; the security test asserts a live conversation + its US-071 token survive their key's revocation.)*
- [x] First key issuance triggers lazy bot provisioning (US-069). *(`_ensure_workspace_bot` is the single, idempotent, best-effort hook invoked on issuance, calling US-069's `provision_workspace_bot(workspace_id, http=...)` - live, since US-069 is on `main` (the branch rebased onto it). Best-effort by design: a provisioning failure is logged and never blocks key issuance, and US-069 also provisions lazily at first conversation (US-078).)*
- [x] `widget_keys` RLS restricts admin reads/writes to admins of the owning workspace (managed in `/support/settings`, US-093). *(SELECT/INSERT/UPDATE policies all gate on `workspace_membership` with `role='admin'`; the security test proves a non-admin member and a non-member read 0 keys and cannot insert/revoke, while the admin can - the only place role legitimately enters a predicate.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes and migration applies. *(`py_compile` clean on `main.py`/`widget_keys.py`/the test; migration applies against the live local Supabase; the app imports and registers all 4 routes.)*
**Validation Test:**
- **Setup:** Workspace W with active key K and revoked key Kr; a live conversation C started under Kr before revocation.
- **Steps:** 1. Resolve K ‚Üí start conversation. 2. Resolve Kr ‚Üí attempt to start conversation. 3. Send a customer message on the pre-existing C (started under Kr).
- **Expected Result:** Step 1 succeeds; step 2 rejected (no new conversation, no minting); step 3 still works (live conversation survives revocation).
- **Failure Indicator:** A revoked key mints a session, or revoking a key kills an in-flight conversation.

### US-073: Per-key registered-domain allowlist, fail-closed (no domain = inactive)
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done (merged to `main` via PR #37, squash commit `1aabd0c`) - `backend/widget_keys.py:is_origin_allowed(origin, allowed_origins)` is the pure, always-unit-testable origin matcher; `main.py`'s `widget_resolve_key` (`POST /widget/keys/resolve`) reads the request `Origin` header and calls it as a SECOND gate layered AFTER the US-072 not-revoked `_resolve_widget_key` check, refusing with the SAME opaque 404 (`"unknown or inactive widget key"`) so an unlisted origin, an originless request, and an empty/null allowlist are all indistinguishable from a revoked/unknown key (nothing leaks whether the key exists or which origins it permits). The matcher is **fail-closed by construction**: an empty `[]` OR null `allowed_origins` makes the key INACTIVE (a key with no registered origin resolves nothing), and a missing OR blank/whitespace `Origin` is refused (the cross-origin widget always sends one - absence means refuse, even under the wildcard). Comparison is **exact, un-normalized string membership** (scheme+host[+port], no path/trailing slash - exactly the form the browser emits), so any casing/slash/port mismatch fails CLOSED (the safe direction for a defense-in-depth gate). `"*"` is a documented **DEV-ONLY** opt-in (PRD F3 row, non-production) that matches any *present* origin but still refuses an originless request. This is **defense-in-depth, NOT a hard control**: the `public_key` is non-secret and `Origin` is trivially forgeable off-browser, so it only blunts casual key-lifting and in-browser cross-site abuse - the hard abuse controls remain the rate limit + circuit breaker (US-076/077) and the leaked-key blast radius is the already-public KB. **No new migration** - `allowed_origins text[]` already existed from US-072's `20260624130000_widget_keys.sql`; the not-revoked gate (`_resolve_widget_key`) stays FIRST and the origin gate is ordered after it. US-078 (server-side re-resolution at conversation creation) reuses this same `is_origin_allowed` helper rather than re-deriving the rule. Test: `python -m backend.test_us073_widget_key_origin` - a unit matcher layer (always runs, security-critical: listed allowed / unlisted refused / empty `[]` + null allowlist refused / missing+blank+whitespace Origin refused / `"*"` allows any present origin alone or mixed / `"*"` still refuses an originless request / exact-match so trailing-slash+case+port mismatches fail closed) plus an endpoint integration layer driving the real `POST /widget/keys/resolve` through a FastAPI TestClient with the US-072 resolve gate mocked (the origin gate lives in the endpoint, not the DB). Shipped through the no-mistakes gate (review + tests + green CI on PR #37).
**Description:** As a security-conscious operator, I want each widget key to carry a registered-origin allowlist that is **fail-closed** (a key with no registered domain is inactive) so that casual key-lifting and cross-site browser abuse are blunted as defense-in-depth (ADR-0008; not a hard control ‚Äî key is non-secret, `Origin` is forgeable off-browser).
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] Resolution checks the request `Origin` against the key's `allowed_origins`; a request from an unlisted origin is refused. *(`widget_resolve_key` reads `request.headers.get("origin")` and calls `is_origin_allowed` after the not-revoked `_resolve_widget_key` gate; an unlisted origin returns the opaque 404 - the integration layer's step 2 (`A` + `https://evil.example` ‚Üí 404) pins it against `is_origin_allowed(OTHER, [LISTED]) is False`.)*
- [x] A key with `allowed_origins` empty/null is **inactive** (fail-closed, same posture as the embedder "refuse to start" guard); never fail-open. *(`is_origin_allowed` returns False on `not allowed_origins` - catching both `[]` and `None`; the unit layer asserts empty + null fail closed and integration step 3 resolves key B (empty allowlist) ‚Üí 404 inactive with or without an Origin.)*
- [x] `*` wildcard is a documented dev-only opt-in, flagged non-production (F3 row). *(`WILDCARD_ORIGIN = "*"` in `widget_keys.py`, documented DEV-ONLY/non-production; it matches any present origin (alone or mixed) yet still refuses an originless request - the unit layer pins both and integration key C admits any origin but 404s without one.)*
- [x] Code/docs frame this as defense-in-depth; the hard controls remain the rate limit + circuit breaker (US-076/077) and the leaked-key blast radius = already-public KB. *(The `is_origin_allowed` docstring, the `widget_resolve_key` endpoint docstring, and the US-073 note in `AGENTS.md`/`CLAUDE.md` all frame it as defense-in-depth-NOT-a-hard-control, naming US-076/077 as the hard controls and the already-public KB as the blast radius.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes. *(`py_compile` clean on `widget_keys.py`/`main.py`/the test; the unit matcher layer and the FastAPI-TestClient endpoint layer both pass; shipped through the no-mistakes gate with green CI on PR #37.)*
**Validation Test (security-critical):**
- **Setup:** Key A with `allowed_origins=['https://client.example']`; key B with empty allowlist.
- **Steps:** 1. Resolve A with `Origin: https://client.example`. 2. Resolve A with `Origin: https://evil.example`. 3. Resolve B (no domain).
- **Expected Result:** Step 1 succeeds; step 2 **rejected**; step 3 **rejected** (inactive, fail-closed).
- **Failure Indicator:** An originless key is active, or an unlisted origin resolves successfully.

### US-074: Public widget CORS posture (separate from `FRONTEND_ORIGINS`)
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done (merged to `main` via PR #40) - the single global `CORSMiddleware(allow_origins=FRONTEND_ORIGINS)` is replaced by **two complementary, path-scoped CORS layers** on one app (`backend/main.py`): an **authenticated** posture (`_ScopedCORSMiddleware(owns_widget=False, allow_origins=FRONTEND_ORIGINS, ‚Ä¶)`) that owns everything NOT a public widget route (`/api/*`, `/healthz`, ‚Ä¶) and keeps EXACTLY the prior posture (same origins/methods/`allow_headers=["*"]`), and a **public-widget** posture (`_WidgetCORSMiddleware`, owns `/widget/*`) that trusts ONLY origins registered on an ACTIVE (not-revoked) widget key - the union of every `widget_keys.allowed_origins` - and NEVER `FRONTEND_ORIGINS`. The partition is the single predicate `_is_widget_public_path(path)` so the two layers are guaranteed complementary (exactly one posture owns each request; no double `Access-Control-Allow-Origin`, no gap). `_WidgetCORSMiddleware` subclasses Starlette's `CORSMiddleware` and overrides `is_allowed_origin` to consult a TTL-cached snapshot (`_WIDGET_ORIGIN_SNAPSHOT`, default 30s `WIDGET_CORS_ORIGIN_CACHE_TTL`, invalidated immediately on key issue/revoke) of the active-key origin union loaded by `_load_active_widget_origins` under the service role; it constructs with `allow_origins=()` so the reflected ACAO is ALWAYS the specific request Origin, **never the literal `*`** (even the dev-only `"*"` key opt-in only widens WHICH origins are admitted, never the reflected value). The snapshot loader FAILS CLOSED - service-role unset or an upstream error returns `(empty, False)` so the surface denies every origin rather than fail-open - and `allows()` mirrors US-073's `is_origin_allowed` rules (missing/blank Origin refused even under `"*"`; exact, un-normalized membership; trailing-slash/case/port mismatch closed). CORS here is BROWSER-side defense-in-depth, NOT the hard boundary: a preflight carries no body so the layer can only answer "is this Origin registered for SOME active key" - the authoritative per-key origin gate (US-073) + not-revoked gate (US-072) + rate limit (US-076) run in the endpoints under the real `public_key`. Authenticated `/widget/*` routes are excluded from the public partition via `_WIDGET_AUTHENTICATED_SUFFIXES` (currently `("/agent-reply",)`) so US-082's agent-reply (authed by the agent's real JWT, called from the operator dashboard on an APP origin) lands on the authenticated posture rather than being CORS-blocked by the per-key allowlist. Test: `python -m backend.test_us074_widget_cors` (unit + loader + a FastAPI-TestClient integration layer encoding the PRD validation test; the widget-origin loader is mocked since the dynamic allowlist lives in the app, not the DB). Note: a disallowed preflight origin yields Starlette's standard 400 "Disallowed CORS origin" with NO `Access-Control-Allow-Origin` (the operative, browser-enforced rejection) rather than a literal 403 - functionally the "reject" the AC calls for; the test asserts on the ACAO absence (the real contract), not the status code.
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] Public widget routes (key resolution, conversation create/message, transcript, customer SSE) are mounted under a distinct CORS configuration keyed off the per-key `allowed_origins`, NOT the global `CORSMiddleware(allow_origins=FRONTEND_ORIGINS)` used by `/api/*`. *(`_WidgetCORSMiddleware` owns `/widget/*` and resolves allowed origins from the active-key `allowed_origins` union via `_WIDGET_ORIGIN_SNAPSHOT`, not `FRONTEND_ORIGINS`.)*
- [x] The authenticated `/api/*` CORS config is unchanged (no widening of `FRONTEND_ORIGINS`). *(`_ScopedCORSMiddleware(owns_widget=False, ‚Ä¶)` keeps the exact prior `allow_origins=FRONTEND_ORIGINS`, methods, and `allow_headers=["*"]`; the integration test confirms `/api/chat` still admits the app origin and rejects a widget origin.)*
- [x] Preflight (`OPTIONS`) on public endpoints reflects only the requesting key's allowed origin (or 403 when not allowed), never `*` outside dev opt-in. *(A registered origin is echoed verbatim in ACAO; a disallowed origin gets NO ACAO - Starlette's standard 400, not 403, but the browser-enforced rejection is the absent ACAO. `allow_origins=()` means the reflected value is never literal `*`, even under the dev-only `"*"` key opt-in.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes. *(`py_compile` clean on `main.py` + the test; `flake8 --select=F` clean - no new undefined/unused; `mypy main.py` adds zero new errors over the pre-existing baseline. Unit + loader + TestClient integration layers all pass.)*
**Validation Test (security-critical):**
- **Setup:** `FRONTEND_ORIGINS=['https://app.kit']`; key K allows `https://client.example`.
- **Steps:** 1. Preflight a public widget endpoint with `Origin: https://client.example`. 2. Preflight same with `Origin: https://app.kit` (not in K's list). 3. Preflight `/api/chat` with `Origin: https://client.example`.
- **Expected Result:** Step 1 allowed (key origin); step 2 rejected (not K's origin even though it's an app origin); step 3 rejected (`/api/*` only trusts `FRONTEND_ORIGINS`).
- **Failure Indicator:** The public surface trusts `FRONTEND_ORIGINS`, or `/api/*` trusts a widget origin.

### US-075: Swappable `RateLimiter` seam (default Postgres, optional Redis adapter)
**Description:** As the platform, I want a `RateLimiter` ABC + factory with a Postgres-backed default (no new infra, durable, cross-instance) and an optional Redis adapter so that abuse counters mirror the existing `Reranker`/`WebSearchProvider`/`DocumentParser` factory pattern (ADR-0008).
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] A `RateLimiter` protocol/ABC with a Postgres implementation (counter rows / sliding-window in Postgres) selected by env (e.g. `RATE_LIMITER=postgres|redis`), default `postgres`.
- [x] An optional Redis adapter stub implementing the same protocol (documented for scale); in-process memory rejected (per-instance under-count, resets on restart) ‚Äî recorded in comment per ADR-0008.
- [x] Migration adds the Postgres counter table(s) the default backend needs.
- [x] Factory shape matches existing seams in the repo.
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes and migration applies.
**Validation Test:**
- **Setup:** `RATE_LIMITER=postgres`.
- **Steps:** 1. Increment a counter for key Z N times within the window. 2. Restart the backend process. 3. Read the counter for Z.
- **Expected Result:** Counter survives the restart at value N (durable, not in-process); selecting `redis` swaps the adapter with no call-site change.
- **Failure Indicator:** Counter resets on restart, or swapping the adapter requires editing call sites.
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done (merged to `main` via PR #41) - `backend/rate_limiting.py` is the swappable seam mirroring the `reranking`/`web_search`/`parsing` factories: a `RateLimiter` ABC (`hit` -> `RateLimitDecision{allowed,count,limit,window_seconds}`, `count` peek, `aclose`) selected by `RATE_LIMITER=postgres|redis` (default `postgres`) via `get_rate_limiter_name()` + `build_rate_limiter()`, which fail-closes at build time on missing config (postgres needs `http` + `SUPABASE_URL` + `SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY`; redis needs `REDIS_URL` + the optional `redis` package, lazily imported with a clear actionable error - `redis` is deliberately NOT added to `requirements.txt`). There is intentionally **NO in-memory backend**: it would under-count per replica and reset on restart, silently disabling the cost-DoS guard (recorded in the module docstring per ADR-0008). `PostgresRateLimiter` (default) reaches counters over PostgREST through two SECURITY DEFINER RPCs, the same backend-mediated/service-role-only posture as US-071's `resume_conversation`. Migration `supabase/migrations/20260624170000_rate_limit_counters.sql` adds `rate_limit_counters(bucket_key, window_seconds, window_start, count, pk(bucket_key,window_seconds,window_start))` - `window_seconds` is part of the row identity so the same key under two different window sizes never conflates and the window-relative prune stays scoped to one (key, window), so the Postgres and Redis backends isolate by (key, window) identically (Redis already namespaces via `{prefix}:{key}:{window_seconds}`) - with **RLS enabled and ZERO policies** (anon/authenticated denied wholesale) plus `rate_limit_hit(p_key,p_limit,p_window_seconds,p_cost default 1)` / `rate_limit_count(p_key,p_window_seconds)` - revoked from `public, anon, authenticated` by name then granted to `service_role` ONLY (Supabase default-privileges gotcha; verified `has_function_privilege('anon',‚Ä¶)=false` and a live anon RPC call returns `42501 permission denied`). The algorithm is the textbook two-bucket **sliding-window counter** (current bucket's exact count + previous bucket weighted by its remaining overlap), bounded to ‚â§2 live rows per (key, window) via an opportunistic in-RPC prune (no per-hit row growth - it would amplify writes under the very abuse it dampens); the Redis adapter mirrors the same weighting on its own clock (a documented cross-instance-skew approximation) with `2*window` key TTLs and a Lua incr+read for atomicity. This story ships ONLY the seam + migration; wiring it onto the widget endpoints (per-key + per-session/IP windows) is US-076 and the per-workspace circuit breaker is US-077 - so the seam has no call site yet by design, and "swap is call-site-free" is structural (every caller talks only to the ABC; the factory `name` flip is the only change). Test: `python -m backend.test_us075_rate_limiter` - a unit layer (always runs: factory default/selection + normalization, no-in-memory rejection, fail-closed config, redis lazy-import error, decision shape + ABC abstractness + both backends sharing the protocol, the Postgres backend's RPC bodies/response parsing over an httpx `MockTransport`, the Redis backend's sliding math over a fake client) + an integration layer (skips cleanly without local Supabase) encoding the PRD validation test: increment key Z 5√ó ‚Üí a FRESH limiter + client (simulated restart) reads Z back at 5 (durable, not in-process), and the limit decision flips `allowed` True‚ÜíFalse past the window. Verified against a local Supabase (CLI 2.90.0): migration applies via `db reset`, all unit + integration assertions pass, and the deny-all/service-role-only boundary holds at the live PostgREST layer.

### US-076: Per-key + per-session/IP sliding-window rate limit
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done (merged to `main` via PR #42) - the FIRST call site of the US-075 `RateLimiter` seam. `backend/main.py` draws every public-widget request down against TWO sliding windows through the seam via TWO single-window helpers sharing a `_charge_widget_window(bucket_key, *, limit, scope, cost)` core: `_enforce_widget_session_limit(request, *, cost=1)` charges the **per-session/IP** bucket `ip:<session>` (caps one caller hammering across keys) and `_enforce_widget_key_limit(public_key, *, cost=1)` charges the **per-key** bucket `key:<public_key>` (caps aggregate abuse of one key across EVERY session/IP - so a fresh session under a hammered key is still refused), both at `WIDGET_RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW_SECONDS` (default 60s) with limits `WIDGET_RATE_LIMIT_PER_KEY` (300) / `WIDGET_RATE_LIMIT_PER_SESSION` (30), all env-tunable so a low test window exercises the breach path. Each window is its own AND-ed gate (refuse if EITHER is over) and a blocked hit still counts (keeping a hammering caller saturated). The split (vs one `asyncio.gather` over both) lets the endpoint **short-circuit between the windows**: the per-SESSION window is charged FIRST - after the cheap `is_widget_public_key` shape guard (a malformed key is a free 404) but BEFORE the DB resolve - so a session-throttle 429s having done no resolve and written no per-key counter row; the per-KEY window is charged only AFTER the resolve proves the key real. **This closes the US-076-review storage-amplification hole:** a rotating-`wk_pk_<random>`-fake-key attacker stops at the resolve (`None` ‚Üí 404) and never reaches the per-key charge, so it can never mint a permanent `rate_limit_counters` row - only the small, controlled set of keys that actually exist ever get a per-key bucket. The residual unbounded axis is `ip:<spoofed-XFF>` session rows (the off-browser traffic the P5 edge/WAF complement handles); a global TTL/sweeper on `rate_limit_counters` is intentionally left to the US-075 seam (out of US-076 scope). On breach it raises a hard **429** with a `Retry-After` header having done NO costly work (no retrieval/LLM / `{active}` reply). **Fail-OPEN on a limiter-backend error:** `rate_limit_counters` live in the SAME Postgres as the resolve/retrieval path, so `_charge_widget_window` wraps `limiter.hit` in a try/except - ANY backend error logs a concise `widget_rate_limit.limiter_error ‚Ä¶ failing open` warning and ALLOWS the request rather than 500-ing the entire public widget surface on a transient counter-RPC glitch (the limiter is not a request-path SPOF; availability wins, edge/WAF is the hard bound), while a genuine over-limit `HTTPException(429)` is raised OUTSIDE the try so it is never swallowed. The throttle is DISTINCT from the US-077 circuit breaker: a 429 "slow down, retry the same request" vs US-077's 200 generic "a human will follow up" deferral; the response body is generic (the tripped scope is logged for ops, never returned, so no per-key/IP topology leaks). Session identity (`_widget_client_ip`) prefers the left-most `X-Forwarded-For` hop (prod sits behind a proxy) falling back to the socket peer - client-spoofable on purpose, so the per-session window is defense-in-depth (a header-rotating attacker is still aggregated by the per-key window, and the edge/WAF limiter is the documented production complement, P5). v1 accounting is COARSE (requests-per-window, `cost`-weighted - the F3 future refinement is precise token/$ metering); `cost` lets US-078's heavier message turn charge more than a cheap open. The limiter is built ONCE at startup via the US-075 factory only when `SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY` is set (fails CLOSED at build time on a misconfigured backend); when support is unconfigured it is `None` and enforcement is a clean no-op - safe because every widget endpoint already 503s before reaching anything costly (a built limiter IS the enforcement). `_on_shutdown` closes the limiter + the long-lived `_RATE_LIMITER_HTTP` client the Postgres backend borrows. Wired onto `POST /widget/keys/resolve` now (per-session first, per-key after the resolve); US-078's first-message flow re-runs the same two helpers (higher `cost`) on the message surface. Test: `python -m backend.test_us076_widget_rate_limit` (unit two-window decision logic against a fake ABC-conforming limiter + a FastAPI-TestClient integration layer encoding the PRD validation test with a fake limiter on `main._RATE_LIMITER` and the resolve gate mocked, limits `per_key == per_session == 3` so the session-first short-circuit isolates each window, plus a per-session-throttle-mints-no-per-key-row assertion and a raising-limiter FAIL-OPEN-not-500 assertion + a helper layer covering both split helpers' no-op and fail-open paths). `ruff check` clean; the only `mypy` findings in `main.py` are pre-existing (OpenAI chat-completions streaming types, lines 1346-1483), none in the US-076 additions.
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] Each customer message / key-resolution request consumes from a per-key window AND a per-session/IP window via the `RateLimiter` seam. *(`_enforce_widget_session_limit` charges `ip:<session>` and `_enforce_widget_key_limit` charges `key:<public_key>` via the US-075 seam, both AND-ed (refuse if EITHER is over); wired onto `POST /widget/keys/resolve` - per-session first, per-key after the resolve - and reused by US-078's message path.)*
- [x] On limit breach the request is refused with a clear throttled response (no retrieval, no LLM call), distinct from the circuit-breaker deferral (US-077). *(A 429 with `Retry-After`, having done no costly work: the per-session gate is raised AFTER the cheap shape guard but BEFORE the DB resolve - the integration test pins that a session-throttle never calls `_resolve_widget_key` and writes no per-key counter row (storage-amplification guard); the per-key gate runs after the cheap resolve existence-check but still before any retrieval/LLM / `{active}` reply. A 429 throttle ‚âÝ US-077's 200 deferral. A limiter-backend error FAILS OPEN, not 500.)*
- [x] Coarse cost accounting in v1 (requests √ó estimated per-request cost, or qps) ‚Äî NOT precise token/dollar metering (documented future refinement, F3). *(Requests-per-window, `cost`-weighted via the seam's `cost` param; precise token/$ metering is documented as the F3 future refinement in the helper docstring + `AGENTS.md`.)*
- [x] App-level limiting is the portable default; an edge/WAF limiter is documented as recommended in production (P5 line). *(The `_widget_client_ip` + `_enforce_widget_session_limit` / `_enforce_widget_key_limit` docstrings and the `AGENTS.md` US-076 note frame app-level limiting as the portable default and name the edge/WAF limiter as the recommended production complement, P5 - also the hard bound when the limiter fails open on a backend error.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes. *(`ruff check` clean on the changed files; `mypy` reports no new findings - the 6 pre-existing errors are all in the unrelated OpenAI chat-completions block, lines 1346-1483.)*
**Validation Test:**
- **Setup:** Key K with a low test window limit; one session S.
- **Steps:** 1. Send messages from S up to the limit. 2. Send one more from S. 3. Send from a fresh session S2 under the same key past the per-key window.
- **Expected Result:** Step 2 throttled (per-session); step 3 throttled by the per-key window even from a new session.
- **Failure Indicator:** No retrieval/LLM call is short-circuited on breach, or only one of the two windows enforces.
- **Result:** ‚úÖ Encoded in `backend/test_us076_widget_rate_limit.py` (integration layer, low test limits per_key == per_session == 3 - equal because the session-first short-circuit means a session-throttle no longer pre-increments the per-key counter): 3 requests from session S (one `X-Forwarded-For` IP) -> 200 (key at 3); the 4th from S -> 429 (per-session, charged FIRST so it does NO resolve and leaves the per-key counter untouched - isolating the session window and proving a session-throttle mints no per-key counter row); a FRESH session S2 -> 429 (per-key window enforces even from a new session whose own session window is fresh; the per-key path DOES run the cheap resolve existence-check once but reaches no retrieval/LLM / `{active}`, isolating the key window); a throttle is verified to be a 429-with-`Retry-After`, never a 200; and a limiter whose `hit()` raises FAILS OPEN (200, not a 500). Both failure indicators - plus the storage-amplification and SPOF regressions from the US-076 review - are directly asserted against.

### US-077: Per-workspace circuit breaker ‚Üí zero-cost deferral + operator Realtime badge
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done (merged to `main` via PR #43) - `backend/circuit_breaker.py` is the per-WORKSPACE breaker, orthogonal to US-076's per-key/per-session windows: it draws down the SAME US-075 `RateLimiter` seam on a distinct `ws:<workspace_id>` bucket (no new store, no new migration - it reuses `rate_limit_counters`), with the MEANING of "per-workspace ceiling" living here and the seam still only counting. `check_workspace_breaker(limiter, workspace_id, *, limit, window_seconds, cost=1) -> BreakerDecision{tripped,count,limit,window_seconds}` charges the bucket and reports `tripped = not allowed`; a blocked hit still counts (a hammering workspace stays tripped, a backed-off one recovers as the window slides). It inherits US-076's two safety stances but is even more clearly fail-OPEN: a NO-OP (never trips) when the limiter is `None` (support unconfigured - the widget endpoints 503 before anything costly), and FAIL-OPEN (never trips) on ANY limiter-backend error - a breaker failing CLOSED would defer a workspace's ENTIRE traffic (a self-inflicted DoS), so a transient counter-RPC glitch must never convert every turn into a deferral. `run_breaker_guarded_turn(*, limiter, workspace_id, limit, window_seconds, run_turn, on_trip=None, cost=1) -> GuardedTurnResult` is the control-flow seam US-079 will call: it checks the breaker FIRST and, when tripped, NEVER awaits the injected `run_turn` thunk - so the (paid) ADR-0003 deflection pipeline makes **zero retrieval and zero LLM calls** (the short-circuit is structural, not a flag the pipeline checks partway through) - returns the generic `GENERIC_BREAKER_DEFERRAL` with `turn=None` (no partial/garbage answer), and fires the optional `on_trip` escalation hook. **Escalate, don't "resolve":** a tripped breaker is a human HANDOFF - `on_trip` (US-080 wires it to the US-067 status latch, a plain DB write) sets the conversation to `escalated`/`escalated_at`, so by the derivable deflection metric (`resolved AND escalated_at IS NULL` => deflected) it reads as human-handled and is therefore NEVER counted as a deflection. **Operator badge = in-app Realtime, zero outbound:** "emit a badge" is not an outbound call - the trip escalates the conversation in Postgres and the operator dashboard (US-087 `/support/queue`) watches `status='escalated'` live via the agent's OWN Supabase Realtime `postgres_changes` under the agent's real JWT (same posture as escalation-notify); no ESP, no webhook, no Slack. The customer-facing `GENERIC_BREAKER_DEFERRAL` is generic ON PURPOSE (it promises a human and leaks NOTHING operational - no workspace id, no counts, no "rate limited"/"breaker"/"ceiling"), differing from the retrieval/faithfulness deferral only in user-facing framing ("high volume" per the PRD wording). `main.py` wires it in: new env knobs `WIDGET_BREAKER_PER_WORKSPACE` (default 600, deliberately ABOVE organic single-workspace traffic - a cost-runaway backstop, not the everyday throttle) and `WIDGET_BREAKER_WINDOW_SECONDS` (defaults to the US-076 window) feed `_check_workspace_breaker(workspace_id, *, cost=1) -> BreakerDecision`, which delegates to the module against the SAME `_RATE_LIMITER` US-076 built once at startup. Like the US-075 seam this story ships the breaker + the guarded runner + `_check_workspace_breaker` with **NO live call site yet by design** - the message-turn runtime (US-078 lazy conversation create / US-079 deflection streaming / US-080 escalation latch) invokes `run_breaker_guarded_turn` on the message path with a real turn thunk + the escalation write as `on_trip`. Test: `python -m backend.test_us077_circuit_breaker` - a unit layer (always runs, no DB/app import: the breaker trips once the ceiling is exceeded on the `ws:` bucket, a blocked hit still counts, no-op-when-`None` and fail-open-on-backend-error both never trip; `run_breaker_guarded_turn` runs the turn + no escalation when un-tripped, and when tripped the central assertion that `run_turn` is NEVER called - 0 retrieval/LLM - plus `turn is None`, the generic deferral, and `on_trip` fired exactly once; the deferral leaks no operational detail; `BreakerDecision` frozen + the fake conforms to the US-075 ABC) plus a helper/integration layer (skips cleanly if the app can't import: `main._check_workspace_breaker` trips past a low test ceiling on the `ws:` bucket, is a clean no-op when unconfigured, and fails open on a backend error). `ruff check` clean on the changed files; `mypy backend/circuit_breaker.py` clean and `mypy backend/main.py` reports no new findings (the pre-existing OpenAI chat-completions streaming + plan-union errors, lines ~1346-1512, are unchanged).
**Description:** As the platform, I want a per-workspace cost/qps circuit breaker that, when tripped, short-circuits to a generic deferral with NO retrieval and NO LLM call plus an in-app Realtime operator badge (zero outbound) so that a tripped breaker costs ~nothing (ADR-0008; same posture as escalation-notify).
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] A per-workspace ceiling (coarse qps/cost) tracked via the `RateLimiter` seam; when tripped, the turn returns a generic "high volume ‚Äî a human will follow up" deferral with **no retrieval and no LLM call**. *(`circuit_breaker.check_workspace_breaker` charges the `ws:<workspace_id>` bucket via the US-075 seam; `run_breaker_guarded_turn` short-circuits the injected `run_turn` thunk when tripped - the unit test asserts `run_turn` is NEVER called on a trip, i.e. 0 retrieval/0 LLM - and returns `GENERIC_BREAKER_DEFERRAL`. Ceiling is env-tunable: `WIDGET_BREAKER_PER_WORKSPACE` / `WIDGET_BREAKER_WINDOW_SECONDS`.)*
- [x] Tripping emits an in-app Realtime operator badge under the agent's real JWT ‚Äî **zero outbound** (no ESP, no webhook), same posture as escalation-notify. *(The `on_trip` hook escalates the conversation (US-080 latch, a plain Postgres write); the operator dashboard reads `status='escalated'` live via the agent's own Supabase Realtime `postgres_changes` (US-087) - no ESP/webhook/Slack anywhere in the path. The hook is injected so US-080 supplies the concrete escalation write; the breaker module fires it exactly when tripped.)*
- [x] A tripped breaker does NOT create a partial/garbage answer and does NOT count as a deflection. *(`GuardedTurnResult.turn is None` when tripped (no fabricated answer - asserted), and escalating sets `escalated_at` so the derivable metric `resolved AND escalated_at IS NULL` reads it as human-handled, never a deflection.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes. *(`ruff check` clean; `mypy backend/circuit_breaker.py` clean; no new `mypy` findings in `main.py`.)*
**Validation Test:**
- **Setup:** Workspace W with a low test per-workspace ceiling; instrument retrieval + LLM call counters.
- **Steps:** 1. Drive W past the ceiling. 2. Send another customer message. 3. Observe operator dashboard for W.
- **Expected Result:** Step 2 returns the generic deferral; retrieval-call and LLM-call counters do NOT increment for that turn; step 3 shows a Realtime badge; no outbound network call is made.
- **Failure Indicator:** A tripped breaker still calls retrieval/LLM, or emits an outbound notification.
- **Result:** ‚úÖ Encoded in `backend/test_us077_circuit_breaker.py`. The `run_turn` thunk doubles as the instrumented retrieval+LLM counter: after driving W past a low test ceiling, the guarded turn returns the generic deferral with the counter still at 0 (the central "retrieval/LLM do NOT increment" assertion - the failure indicator directly asserted against), fires the `on_trip` escalation hook exactly once (the in-app Realtime badge; zero outbound is structural - no network client is ever touched on the trip path), and returns `turn=None` (no partial answer). The complementary not-tripped case proves the turn DOES run and does NOT escalate. The live end-to-end dashboard observation lands with the operator queue (US-087) and the message-turn call site (US-078‚Äì080), which this seam is built ready for - mirroring how US-075 shipped its seam ahead of US-076's call site.

### US-078: Lazy conversation creation on first customer message
**Description:** As the platform, I want a `conversations` row + opaque customer token + customer SSE created **lazily on the first customer message**, NOT on widget open, so that the public-page abuse surface is bounded to one-row-per-real-conversation (ADR-0008; CONTEXT lifecycle).
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done (merged to `main` via PR #44) - `POST /widget/conversations/messages` (`main.py:widget_conversation_message`) is the customer message surface. A `conversations` row + its opaque token (US-071) are born ONLY on the first real customer message; widget OPEN does ONLY rate-limited key resolution (`POST /widget/keys/resolve`), so a merely-loaded page / crawler creates ZERO rows. The endpoint branches on the presence of the `X-Conversation-Token` header (not a flag): no token => FIRST MESSAGE (re-run the US-072 not-revoked + US-073 origin gates server-side via the SAME helpers as `/widget/keys/resolve`, idempotent `_ensure_workspace_bot` US-069, `_create_widget_conversation` service-role INSERT with `status='active'` + `bot_user_id` + `channel='widget'`, then `_issue_conversation_token` US-071); token present => RESUME (`_resume_conversation_by_token` resolves it to its ONE bound conversation iff not-expired AND not-resolved, creating NO row - a reload never duplicates; miss -> 401). The customer message is persisted to `conversation_messages` (role='user', `tool_calls` null) before the SSE opens. The raw token is returned EXACTLY ONCE in the `X-Conversation-Token` RESPONSE HEADER (never an SSE event / body / log - US-071), and US-074's widget CORS posture now `expose_headers`-es it so the cross-origin iframe can read it once; a resume mints no new token. The response is the request-scoped SSE the bot answer streams over in US-079 (like `/api/chat`) - this story OPENS it and emits a `conversation` event then `done`; the deflection pipeline + delta streaming (US-079), escalation latch (US-080), and long-lived async-reply SSE (US-081) are deliberately out of scope (the codebase framing: "US-078 lazy conversation create / US-079 deflection streaming / US-080 escalation latch"). Backend-mediated under the service role (same posture as US-071), NO new migration (writes the US-066 tables as-is); `escalated_at` is never planted by the caller (US-067 trigger owns it). Rate-limited via US-076 at the heavier `WIDGET_RATE_LIMIT_MESSAGE_COST` (default 5): per-session FIRST on both branches, per-key only after the first-message resolve. Test: `python -m backend.test_us078_lazy_conversation` (unit payload builders + a FastAPI-TestClient integration layer encoding the validation test with every DB helper mocked). `ruff` clean on the changed files; `mypy main.py` reports no new findings (the pre-existing OpenAI chat-completions streaming + plan-union errors, lines ~1390-1527, are unchanged).
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] Widget open performs ONLY rate-limited key resolution ‚Äî no `conversations` row, no customer token, no SSE. *(`POST /widget/keys/resolve` is side-effect-free; the validation test asserts 5 opens create 0 rows.)*
- [x] The first customer message creates the `conversations` row (`status='active'`, `bot_user_id` set, `channel='widget'`), issues the opaque token (US-071), opens the customer SSE, and runs the ADR-0003 pipeline. *(Row created active/widget with `bot_user_id` from US-069, opaque token issued via `_issue_conversation_token` and returned once in the response header, and the request-scoped SSE is OPENED here. The ADR-0003 deflection pipeline RUN + answer streaming over that SSE is US-079's scope, and the long-lived async-reply customer SSE is US-081 - left to those stories per the codebase's own split; this story opens the SSE shell and announces the conversation.)*
- [x] Reload with a valid stored token resumes the existing conversation (US-071) rather than creating a new row. *(Token-bearing message -> `_resume_conversation_by_token`, no INSERT; the validation test asserts step 3 stays at 1 row.)*
- [x] No "row per pageview" ‚Äî repeated opens without a message create zero rows. *(Validation test step 1: 5 opens -> 0 rows.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes. *(`ruff check` clean; `mypy main.py` no new findings.)*
**Validation Test:**
- **Setup:** Fresh widget key K, no stored token.
- **Steps:** 1. Resolve K (open) 5 times without sending a message ‚Üí count `conversations` rows. 2. Send first message ‚Üí count rows. 3. Reload with stored token, send second message ‚Üí count rows.
- **Expected Result:** Step 1 ‚Üí 0 rows; step 2 ‚Üí 1 row; step 3 ‚Üí still 1 row (resumed, not duplicated).
- **Failure Indicator:** Any row created on open, or a reload duplicates the conversation.

### US-079: Deterministic deflection turn streams over the request-scoped SSE
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done (merged to `main` via PR #45) - `main.py:widget_conversation_message`'s SSE generator now runs the customer turn AS the workspace bot and streams the result. After the `conversation` event it calls `_run_widget_bot_turn` (the single deflection-turn seam), persists the bot reply to `conversation_messages` (role='assistant', `tool_calls` null), and streams it as `delta` events then `done` - reusing the EXACT `_sse()` `delta`/`done`/`error` shape `/api/chat` uses. `_run_widget_bot_turn` runs `support_bot.run_bot_deflection_turn` (US-070) behind `circuit_breaker.run_breaker_guarded_turn` (US-077's FIRST live call site - the cost backstop goes live with the paid pipeline) against the SAME `_RATE_LIMITER`, with the ONE validated `_ESCALATION_CONFIG = EscalationConfig.from_env()` (US-050, built at startup) + `get_similarity_threshold()`; it returns only the client-safe `customer_message` (the minted bot JWT never leaves `support_bot`). It is FAIL-CLOSED: a botless workspace (US-078 leaves `bot_user_id` nullable, incl. a transient service-role failure loading a resumed conversation's `bot_user_id`), an unimportable support module, a missing `SUPABASE_JWT_SECRET`, a tripped breaker, or any pipeline error all stream the fixed generic deferral, never a confident answer - the botless short-circuit returns before any import/mint/LLM. Streaming is REPLAY-chunking via `_split_for_streaming` (byte-exact reassembly), forced by the ADR-0003 design: the faithfulness gate (US-048) verifies the WHOLE draft before it may send, so the answer cannot be streamed token-by-token live. The bot reply is persisted BEFORE the deltas stream (transcript durability; a persist failure emits an `error` event, no deltas); the generator also re-checks `request.is_disconnected()` immediately before the paid turn, so a client that already dropped incurs zero retrieval/LLM (a per-request cost trim atop the breaker). A RESUMED conversation reads `bot_user_id` under the service role (`_load_conversation_bot_user_id`, itself fail-closed - a transient read error returns None and escalates rather than raising) since the US-071 `resume_conversation` RPC's customer view omits it (avoids a DROP/recreate of the security-DEFINER RPC). **SCOPE BOUNDARY** (per the codebase's own split): US-079 streams the turn and leaves the conversation `active` on every branch; the escalation LATCH (`status='escalated'`/`escalated_at`), the breaker's `on_trip` escalation write, and the "skip the pipeline once escalated" routing are ALL US-080 (criterion 3's "triggers the latch (US-080)" is the streamed-deferral handoff cue; the DB latch write itself is US-080). Test: `python -m backend.test_us079_deflection_streaming` (unit: byte-exact chunker, botless short-circuit, `tool_calls`-null payload; integration via FastAPI TestClient with the DB helpers + the ADR-0003 pipeline mocked: answered streams+persists user/assistant, escalate streams the deferral, a tripped breaker runs ZERO pipeline calls, botless escalates, resume resolves the bot and streams). `ruff` clean; `mypy main.py` reports no new findings.
**Description:** As an anonymous customer, I want the bot's own answer to stream over the request-scoped SSE my message opened (like `/api/chat`) so that I get a low-latency answer while `status='active'`, reusing the ADR-0003 deflection pipeline and the existing `_sse()` `delta`/`done`/`error` event shape (`main.py:474`).
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] A customer message on an `active` conversation runs the ADR-0003 deterministic deflection pipeline (retrieval gate ‚Üí [if strong] draft ‚Üí faithfulness gate) ‚Äî implemented by the **escalation-pipeline section**; this story only invokes it and streams the result. *(`_run_widget_bot_turn` invokes `support_bot.run_bot_deflection_turn` behind the US-077 breaker; the pipeline itself is US-047/048/049's.)*
- [x] Bot answer streams over the request-scoped SSE using the existing `_sse()` `delta`/`done`/`error` events; both customer message and bot answer are persisted to `conversation_messages` (face-agnostic streaming/draft/gate service writing to `conversation_messages` instead of `messages`, per ADR-0004 consequence). *(Customer message persisted by US-078 role='user'; bot reply persisted here role='assistant' before the deltas stream; `_split_for_streaming` replays the approved answer as `delta` events then `done`.)*
- [x] On the escalate branch, the pipeline emits no answer (generic deferral) and triggers the latch (US-080) ‚Äî it does not stream a confident answer. *(The escalate branch - weak retrieval, unfaithful draft, tripped breaker, or any failure - streams the fixed generic deferral; the DB latch write is US-080, left `active` here.)*
- [x] `conversation_messages.tool_calls` stays null (deterministic pipeline, no agentic tool loop). *(`_conversation_message_insert_payload` omits the field; pinned by the US-079 unit test.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes. *(`ruff` clean on the changed files; `mypy main.py` adds no new findings beyond the pre-existing ~1406-1543 OpenAI/plan-union errors.)*
**Validation Test:**
- **Setup:** Conversation C `active`; a question whose answer is in a shared-to-bot doc (P2).
- **Steps:** 1. Send the question. 2. Observe the SSE stream and `conversation_messages`.
- **Expected Result:** `delta` events stream a grounded answer then `done`; user + assistant rows persisted to `conversation_messages`; `tool_calls` null.
- **Failure Indicator:** The answer fails to stream over the request SSE, or persists to `messages`/`threads`.

### US-080: Escalation latch routes all later customer messages to the human
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done (merged to `main` via PR #46) - US-080 closes the SCOPE BOUNDARY US-079 left open (a breaker trip was cost-safe but not a recorded handoff) with **no new migration and no new env** - it reuses the US-066 `conversations` table and the US-067 status machine. `main.py:_escalate_conversation` is the SINGLE latch path for BOTH the model-mediated escalate and the explicit "talk to a human" button: a service-role PATCH that sets **ONLY** `status='escalated'` - `escalated_at` is the US-067 trigger's to set-once/preserve (never planted by the caller), which is what keeps deflection derivable. Inside `_run_widget_bot_turn` two DELIBERATE sources latch (best-effort via `_escalate_conversation_safe`): a tripped US-077 breaker - wired as the breaker's `on_trip` hook (US-079 passed `on_trip=None`; this is the hook US-077 shipped for exactly this) - and the pipeline returning `action='escalated'`, latched after the un-tripped turn. The fail-closed DEGRADED deferrals (botless workspace, unimportable `support_bot`, any pipeline error) deliberately do NOT latch - they may be transient, and permanently silencing the bot on a blip would be wrong, so they defer THIS turn and stay `active` to recover (preserving US-079's botless-without-touching-the-pipeline invariant). The in-turn latch is best-effort (a write blip never turns the deferral 200 into a 500; concise warning, no traceback flood); the explicit `POST /widget/conversations/escalate` uses the strict `_escalate_conversation` and surfaces a failure as 502. Routing (AC2): `widget_conversation_message` captures `conversation_status` and the SSE generator short-circuits an already-`escalated` conversation to `conversation` + `done` - the customer message was persisted before the SSE opened (the queue input), the bot stays silent, the human reply arrives over the US-081 SSE; the resume branch also skips the `_load_conversation_bot_user_id` read once escalated. The FIRST escalating turn still runs the pipeline (to get the decision + emit the deferral) and latches as a side effect; only LATER messages skip. The explicit button (AC3, US-091's caller) is token-authed (US-071 opaque `X-Conversation-Token`, NOT a Supabase JWT), per-session rate-limited (US-076), runs NO pipeline (UI-initiated, never a model tool), and inherits US-074's public-widget CORS posture. Test: `python -m backend.test_us080_escalation_latch` (unit: the PATCH sets status and NEVER `escalated_at`, pinned via an httpx `MockTransport`; `_run_widget_bot_turn` latches a model escalate AND a tripped breaker via `on_trip` with ZERO pipeline calls, but NOT a confident answer or a botless degraded deferral; integration via FastAPI TestClient with the DB helpers + pipeline mocked, encoding the PRD validation test: first escalate latches `status='escalated'`/`escalated_at` once + streams the deferral, the two later messages persist + queue with the pipeline-entry counter NOT incrementing and `escalated_at` NOT reset, and the explicit button latches via the same path without running the pipeline). `ruff` clean; `mypy main.py` reports no new findings (pre-existing ~1406-1543 OpenAI/plan-union errors unchanged).
**Description:** As the platform, I want the first escalate decision to latch the conversation to `escalated` (bot goes silent, one-way) so that once a human is engaged the bot can never auto-send a confident wrong answer into the thread (ADR-0004; Risk #3).
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] The first turn whose ADR-0003 decision is escalate sets `status='escalated'` and `escalated_at=now()` (latch via US-067) and emits a generic deferral, not a bot answer. *(`_run_widget_bot_turn` latches via `_escalate_conversation_safe` when the pipeline returns `action='escalated'` OR the US-077 breaker trips (the breaker's `on_trip` hook); the PATCH sets only `status`, the US-067 trigger stamps `escalated_at`; the streamed reply is the generic deferral, never a confident answer.)*
- [x] While `status='escalated'`, every later customer message is persisted to `conversation_messages` and routed to the human queue WITHOUT running the deflection pipeline (no retrieval, no draft, no LLM answer). *(The SSE generator short-circuits a `conversation_status=='escalated'` conversation to `conversation`+`done`; the customer message is persisted before the SSE opens; `_run_widget_bot_turn` is never called. Pinned by the integration test's pipeline-entry counter staying flat across the two later messages.)*
- [x] User-initiated "talk to a human" (an explicit widget button, US-091) escalates via this same latch path ‚Äî separate from the model-mediated decision. *(`POST /widget/conversations/escalate` - token-authed, per-session rate-limited, runs no pipeline - calls the SAME `_escalate_conversation`; US-091 ships the frontend button that calls it.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes. *(`ruff` clean on the changed files; `mypy main.py` adds no new findings beyond the pre-existing ~1406-1543 OpenAI/plan-union errors.)*
**Validation Test:**
- **Setup:** Conversation C `active`; instrument the deflection-pipeline entry.
- **Steps:** 1. Send a message that escalates (or click the human button). 2. Send two more customer messages. 3. Inspect pipeline-entry counter for steps 2's messages.
- **Expected Result:** After step 1, `status='escalated'`, `escalated_at` set; step 2 messages persist and appear in the queue but the pipeline-entry counter does NOT increment for them.
- **Failure Indicator:** Bot re-answers after escalation, or `escalated_at` is reset/unset on later turns.

### US-081: Customer SSE channel + LISTEN/NOTIFY fan-out
**Description:** As an anonymous customer, I want a long-lived backend SSE (authorized by my opaque token) over which async agent replies are pushed so that I receive a human reply without ever holding a Supabase JWT or touching Supabase Realtime ‚Äî single-instance trivial, multi-instance via Postgres `LISTEN/NOTIFY` (no new infra) (ADR-0008; amends ADR-0004).
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done (local; pending the no-mistakes gate / PR) - the customer leg's live push, completing the seam US-082 left (it shipped the single-instance `ConversationFanout` registry; US-081 adds the consumer + the cross-instance transport). **No new migration, no new table** - `LISTEN`/`NOTIFY` are built-ins; the one new env is the OPTIONAL `WIDGET_FANOUT_DATABASE_URL`.

`GET /widget/conversations/{conversation_id}/events` (`backend/main.py:widget_conversation_events`) is the long-lived customer SSE, authorized by the US-071 OPAQUE token (`X-Conversation-Token`, NOT a Supabase JWT - so the customer is structurally OFF the Supabase Realtime/JWT surface; `EventSource` can't set headers, so the iframe consumes it via fetch + ReadableStream like the POST stream). It resolves the token to its ONE bound conversation with `slide=False` (holding a passive read channel open is not activity that should extend the 24h window - the transcript-read precedent) and enforces the binding (`conv["id"] == path id`), so a token for X can never open Y's stream; a missing/expired/resolved/mismatched token ‚Üí opaque 401. It then drains `_CONVERSATION_FANOUT.subscribe(conversation_id)`, emitting `event: ready` then one `event: message` per agent reply (the customer-safe body only). A `: keepalive` comment every `WIDGET_SSE_KEEPALIVE_SECONDS` (25) survives proxy idle-timeouts; the token is re-validated every `WIDGET_SSE_REVALIDATE_SECONDS` (60, slide=False) and a now-invalid token (the conversation was resolved ‚Üí its token purged, US-071) emits `event: close` and ends - the connection closes when the token is invalidated. The stream uses a PERSISTENT get-task across keepalive timeouts (asyncio.wait leaves it pending) so a reply arriving exactly at a heartbeat boundary is never dropped between iterations. Per-session rate-limited at open (US-076; no `public_key` on this path) as defense-in-depth against SSE-open spam. The route is NOT a `_WIDGET_AUTHENTICATED_SUFFIXES` suffix, so US-074's PUBLIC-widget CORS posture owns it (the anonymous-customer surface).

The multi-instance bridge is `backend/conversation_bridge.py:ConversationBridge` - the OPTIONAL Postgres `LISTEN`/`NOTIFY` transport that feeds INTO the same in-process registry, so the endpoint is identical no matter how many instances run. Built + started at startup ONLY when `WIDGET_FANOUT_DATABASE_URL` (a direct asyncpg DSN for the shared Postgres) is set; unset ‚Üí single-instance fan-out only (the common kit deployment) and the bridge is never built. After the agent-reply endpoint (US-082) durably writes + `publish()`es LOCALLY, it also calls `bridge.notify(conversation_id, event)` (best-effort, non-fatal), which emits a single-channel `NOTIFY` carrying `{origin: <this instance's id>, conversation_id, event}`. Every instance runs a supervised `LISTEN` connection (reconnect with backoff + a health probe so a silently-dropped socket self-heals); on each notification it `publish()`es LOCALLY - EXCEPT a frame stamped with its OWN instance id, which it ignores (the dedup that stops the originating instance double-pushing on top of its local publish). A malformed/foreign frame is dropped, never raised. A NOTIFY payload over `_MAX_NOTIFY_PAYLOAD_BYTES` (7000, under Postgres's 8000 cap) skips the cross-instance nudge (the remote customer recovers via the transcript) - the local publish always delivers in full. The whole bridge is fail-soft: a DB blip degrades to single-instance delivery + the transcript backstop, never crashing a request or startup. NO Redis/queue infra; `workspace_membership.role` appears nowhere (ADR-0002 intact).

Frontend: `frontend/src/widget/api.ts:subscribeConversationEvents` (fetch-based SSE with the token header, parsing `ready`/`message`/`close`) + a `useConversation.ts` effect that holds the SSE open whenever a conversation + token exist, reconnecting on drop, feeding the SAME `refreshTranscript` seam US-084 named (a `message` is a low-latency NUDGE to re-read the durable transcript - the transcript stays the source of truth). The interim transcript POLL is RETAINED as a backstop (a dropped/closed SSE never loses a reply), so the SSE is purely a latency win. No supabase-js channel on the customer leg.

Test: `python -m backend.test_us081_customer_sse` - a BRIDGE unit layer (always runs, no DB/app: the cross-instance envelope round-trips + rejects malformed frames; the LISTEN callback REPLAYS a remote event into the local registry but IGNORES our own instance's frame (dedup) and any malformed/foreign frame, delivering to ONLY the matching conversation) plus an ENDPOINT/STREAM layer (drives the real generator on one loop with the token resolve mocked: a token bound to another conversation ‚Üí 401; the VALIDATION TEST - X's stream delivers ONLY X's reply and a Y reply published meanwhile NEVER reaches it; a resolved-token re-validation closes the stream with `event: close`) plus an HTTP-surface layer (TestClient: missing token ‚Üí 401, cross-binding ‚Üí 401, and the US-074 partition treats the events route as the anonymous public-widget surface). `ruff` clean on the changed files; `mypy backend/conversation_bridge.py` clean except the `asyncpg` import-untyped finding `semantic_layer.py`/`sql_compiler.py` already ship with, and `mypy backend/main.py` reports no new findings (the pre-existing OpenAI streaming + plan-union errors are unchanged); `npm run typecheck` + multi-page `npm run build` clean.
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] A `GET` customer SSE endpoint authorized by the opaque per-conversation token (US-071) holds a long-lived connection scoped to one `conversation_id`. *(`GET /widget/conversations/{id}/events`, token-authed via `_resume_conversation_by_token` + the path-id binding; drains `_CONVERSATION_FANOUT.subscribe(conversation_id)` for the connection's life with keepalive + periodic token re-validation.)*
- [x] A fan-out mechanism delivers a new `conversation_messages` row to the matching customer SSE: single-instance in-process registry; multi-instance uses Postgres `LISTEN/NOTIFY` keyed by `conversation_id` (no Redis/queue infra added). *(The US-082 `ConversationFanout` registry is the single-instance core; `ConversationBridge` adds the optional Postgres LISTEN/NOTIFY transport that publishes INTO the same registry - the payload carries `conversation_id` so `publish` routes only to that conversation's subscribers. No Redis/queue/migration.)*
- [x] The customer SSE never carries any data from other conversations; the connection closes/refuses when the token is invalidated (resolve). *(`publish` delivers only to the exact conversation's subscribers - pinned by the validation test; the in-stream re-validation (slide=False) emits `event: close` and ends when a resolved/expired token resolves to None.)*
- [x] The anonymous customer is structurally OFF the Supabase JWT/Realtime surface (no supabase-js channel for the customer leg). *(The endpoint is authed by the opaque token, never `get_user`/a Supabase JWT; the bridge is plain Postgres LISTEN/NOTIFY; the frontend uses a backend fetch-SSE, never a supabase-js Realtime channel. The events route is the US-074 public-widget (anonymous) surface, asserted in the test.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes. *(`ruff` clean on the changed backend files; `npm run typecheck` + multi-page `npm run build` clean; `mypy` reports no new findings beyond the shared `asyncpg` import-untyped already accepted across the repo.)*
**Validation Test (security-critical):**
- **Setup:** Two conversations X (token Tx), Y (token Ty), possibly on different backend instances.
- **Steps:** 1. Open customer SSE for X with Tx. 2. Insert an agent reply into Y. 3. Insert an agent reply into X.
- **Expected Result:** X's SSE receives ONLY the X reply (step 3); the Y reply (step 2) is **never** delivered to X's SSE (0 cross-conversation messages).
- **Failure Indicator:** X's SSE receives a Y message, or the customer leg subscribes to Supabase Realtime.

### US-082: Agent-reply endpoint (`POST /widget/conversations/{id}/agent-reply`)
**Description:** As a workspace agent, I want `POST /widget/conversations/{id}/agent-reply` (authed by my real workspace JWT) to write `conversation_messages` AND fan the message down the matching customer SSE so that my reply reaches the anonymous customer through the backend, not Supabase Realtime (ADR-0008; amends ADR-0004).
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done (merged to `main` via PR #47) - `POST /widget/conversations/{id}/agent-reply` (`backend/main.py:widget_agent_reply`) is the human leg, the ONE authenticated `/widget/*` route (every other widget endpoint is the anonymous-customer surface authed by the US-071 opaque token). **No new migration, no new env** - it reuses the US-066 `conversations` / `conversation_messages` tables. The boundary is the US-066 workspace-membership RLS enforced UNDER THE AGENT'S OWN JWT (`get_user` + `_supabase_headers(user)`): the endpoint reads the conversation (`_fetch_conversation_for_agent`) and INSERTs the reply (`_insert_agent_reply`) under the agent's token, so a member may reply and a cross-workspace agent is rejected by Postgres - the membership SELECT 404s an RLS-hidden/absent conversation (indistinguishable from not-found, the `_fetch_thread` posture, leaking nothing) and the INSERT's `with check` membership policy is the independent hard write boundary (the DB-layer zero-leak is pinned by `backend/test_us066_conversations_rls.py`). The reply is written `role='assistant'` (the only support-side role the US-066 CHECK allows - `user|assistant|system|tool`; there is no `'agent'` role, so no migration) with `tool_calls` null, exactly as the customer sees it in the US-071 transcript. Replies are permitted regardless of status - in particular on `escalated`, where the bot is silent (US-080) and the agent is the ONLY message source (no status gate; membership RLS is the sole boundary). After the durable write the reply is fanned to the customer's live backend SSE through a NEW in-process registry (`backend/conversation_fanout.py:ConversationFanout`): `_CONVERSATION_FANOUT.publish(conversation_id, message_event(message))` is synchronous + non-blocking (`Queue.put_nowait`, so a slow SSE never stalls the write path), delivers ONLY to subscribers of that exact conversation (the US-081 cross-conversation-isolation property), delivers to 0 when no SSE is open (the reply is still durable in the transcript), and drops on a full queue rather than blocking. The registry holds state only for conversations with an open SSE (an idle backend keeps no per-conversation memory) - keeping the anonymous customer off the Supabase Realtime/JWT surface (ADR-0008 max-isolation). The route ends in `/agent-reply`, already in US-074's `_WIDGET_AUTHENTICATED_SUFFIXES`, so it lands on the authenticated CORS posture (reachable from the dashboard's app origin) with NO CORS change. **SCOPE BOUNDARY:** US-082 ships the endpoint + the registry's `publish`/`subscribe` primitives (the single-instance fan-out US-081's AC lists first); US-081 still owns the customer-facing GET SSE endpoint (token-authed, long-lived, draining `subscribe()`) AND the multi-instance Postgres `LISTEN/NOTIFY` bridge that feeds INTO this same registry (a `notify()` beside `publish()` + a background `LISTEN` task - no Redis/queue infra), the same seam-before-call-site split as US-075‚Üí076 / US-077‚Üí079. Test: `python -m backend.test_us082_agent_reply` (a registry unit layer + a main-helper unit layer via httpx `MockTransport` + a handler/fan-out layer on one event loop + an HTTP-surface layer via FastAPI TestClient, encoding the validation test: A1 member reply writes-under-the-agent's-JWT + fans out to C only, A2 cross-workspace ‚Üí 404 / 0 rows / 0 fan-out, replies permitted on escalated, missing bearer ‚Üí 401). `ruff` clean on the changed files; `mypy backend/conversation_fanout.py` clean and `mypy backend/main.py` reports no new findings (the pre-existing OpenAI streaming + plan-union errors, lines ~1417-1554, are unchanged).
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] Endpoint authed by the agent's real Supabase JWT via the existing `get_user` path; the agent must be a member of the conversation's workspace (membership RLS on the write, US-066). *(`Depends(get_user)`; the read + insert run under `_supabase_headers(user)` so the US-066 membership RLS is the authorization. The PRD's `main.py:361` line ref is stale - `get_user` now lives at ~`main.py:926`.)*
- [x] Writes the `(role='assistant'/'agent', content)` row to `conversation_messages` under the agent's JWT, then triggers the customer-SSE fan-out (US-081) for that `conversation_id`. *(`role='assistant'` - the US-066 CHECK has no `'agent'` role; `_CONVERSATION_FANOUT.publish` fans it to the conversation's subscribers after the durable write. The customer GET SSE endpoint + multi-instance LISTEN/NOTIFY remain US-081, which consumes this registry's `subscribe()`.)*
- [x] Reply is permitted on `escalated` conversations (and is the only message source post-latch); a non-member's JWT is rejected. *(No status gate on the write; a cross-workspace agent's membership read 404s - RLS-hidden - before any write, and the INSERT's `with check` is the independent backstop.)*
- [x] Typecheck/lint passes. *(`ruff` clean; `mypy conversation_fanout.py` clean; `mypy main.py` no new findings.)*
**Validation Test (security-critical):**
- **Setup:** Conversation C in workspace W (`escalated`); agent A1 ‚àà W, agent A2 ‚àâ W; customer SSE open for C.
- **Steps:** 1. A1 posts an agent reply to C. 2. A2 (cross-workspace JWT) posts a reply to C.
- **Expected Result:** Step 1 writes `conversation_messages` and the reply arrives on C's customer SSE; step 2 **rejected / 0 rows written** (A2 not a member of W).
- **Failure Indicator:** A2's cross-workspace reply succeeds, or A1's reply fails to fan out to the customer.

### US-083: Loader `<script>` + cross-origin iframe widget shell (host‚Üîwidget postMessage)
**Description:** As a buyer, I want a tiny loader `<script>` that injects a launcher bubble + a cross-origin iframe served from the kit's own origin, communicating with the host page via `postMessage` only, so that the host page's JS (or an XSS on it) cannot read the widget's token (ADR-0008 max-isolation embed).
**Status:** ‚úÖ Done (merged to `main` via PR #48) - **frontend-only, no backend / migration / env.** The vanilla loader `frontend/public/widget.js` derives the kit origin from its OWN `<script src>` (`new URL('widget.html', selfScript.src)`), so the injected iframe `src` is always the kit's `widget.html` - a DIFFERENT origin from the host - and that cross-origin boundary IS the security control (host reads of `iframe.contentWindow.localStorage`/`document` throw `SecurityError`). It reads non-secret config from `data-*` attributes (`data-public-key` = US-072 `wk_pk_‚Ä¶`, plus `brand-color`/`greeting`/`title`/`position`/`launcher-icon`/`z-index`, overridable via `window.SupportWidgetSettings`; deliberately NO host-supplied `api-base` - the widget talks only to its own build-time backend so a host XSS cannot redirect the token, US-084 security fix), injects a fixed-corner iframe sized bubble (96√ó96, closed) / panel (open), is idempotent, and exposes a TOKEN-FREE `window.SupportWidget` (`open`/`close`/`toggle`/`onUnread`). Host‚Üîwidget is `postMessage` ONLY (contract in `frontend/src/widget/protocol.ts`, hand-duplicated in the loader; channel `ar-support-widget@1`): host‚Üíwidget `init` (config, `targetOrigin` pinned to the kit origin) + `command`; widget‚Üíhost `ready` (only `'*'` send, no secret) + `state` (`{open}`, iframe is the single source of truth, loader resizes off it) + `unread`. Origin checks are strict both ways. The launcher AND panel live INSIDE the iframe (host CSS reaches no pixel); the widget is a separate Vite entry (`frontend/widget.html` ‚Üí `src/widget/main.tsx`, added to `rollupOptions.input`) that never imports the admin app/supabase. Token/session live in the iframe's own-origin `localStorage` via `src/widget/storage.ts` (namespaced by public key; session minted on `init`; the token slot is populated by US-084 from the US-078 header). Web-component/shadow-DOM REJECTED (same JS realm) - noted in `widget.js`/`protocol.ts`/`docs/widget-embed.md`. This is the SHELL only; the in-iframe chat UI + theming render is US-084. Verified in-browser (the validation method for this story; the frontend has no unit-test harness) with the kit on `:5173` and the host fixture `frontend/widget-host-example.html` on `:8099`: cross-origin iframe injected, `init` forwards key + theming (applied), open/close/toggle resize via the `state` round-trip, and with a real token planted in the kit origin the host's reads of the iframe's `localStorage`/`document` BOTH throw `SecurityError`, host storage holds no token, and `SupportWidget` exposes none. `npm run typecheck` + multi-page `npm run build` both clean.
**Acceptance Criteria:**
- [x] A small loader script injects a launcher + an iframe whose `src` is the kit's own origin (NOT the host origin); the conversation token + session live in the iframe's own-origin `localStorage`, unreadable by host JS. *(`widget.js` derives the kit origin from its own `<script src>`; launcher + panel render inside the iframe; `storage.ts` keeps token/session in the iframe origin - host read throws `SecurityError`, verified in-browser.)*
- [x] Host‚Üîwidget communication is `postMessage` only: `open`/`close`, unread-badge, and `init` config ‚Äî no shared globals, no host-CSS reaching the iframe. *(`command`(open/close/toggle) + `state` + `unread` + `init` over the `ar-support-widget@1` channel; the only host global is the token-free `window.SupportWidget`; the cross-origin iframe forecloses host CSS.)*
